Best practice for a UBB platform: partial coverage should be detected and surfaced, never silently dropped — under-billing is as dangerous as over-billing. The clean fix is additive and symmetric to the cost leg, which already collects `uncosted_metrics`: have the price leg collect an `unpriced_metrics` list and return it in `pricing_provenance` (and optionally honour `require_cost_card_coverage`-style strict mode for the price side, refusing the event if some-but-not-all metrics are priced). Effect: no schema change, no hot-path restructure — just populate provenance and optionally raise. This turns a silent revenue leak into a visible, opt-in-enforceable signal.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** If one event carries two billable things and you've only set a price for one of them, UBB charges for that one and quietly charges nothing for the other — a silent revenue leak. The fix is to flag "you priced one but not both" so the customer notices, the same way UBB already flags missing cost data.

- Creating a duplicate ACTIVE rate card (same tenant/customer/type/provider/event_type/metric/dimensions/currency) is not caught at the endpoint — the partial unique constraint raises an unhandled IntegrityError (500, not 422) (ubb-platform/api/v1/metering_endpoints.py:588-604; ubb-platform/apps/metering/pricing/models.py:152-163).

  > **Verified —** True — a real bug. `create_rate_card` calls `RateCard.objects.create(...)` with no try/except (ubb-platform/api/v1/metering_endpoints.py:588-604); the partial unique constraints `uq_ratecard_active_tenant`/`uq_ratecard_active_customer` (ubb-platform/apps/metering/pricing/models.py:152-163) will raise IntegrityError on a duplicate active card, which is unhandled → HTTP 500. (The batch path at metering_endpoints.py:633-655 has the same exposure inside its atomic block.) Confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Orb and Lago both return clean validation errors / 409s on conflicting writes (e.g. Orb's idempotency layer returns 409 on key reuse with a different payload — 03 §2; Lago's uniqueness-key reuse returns 409 — 03 §3 analogue), and reuse returns a documented status, never a 500. A 5xx on a client-caused conflict is a clear competitiveness/quality defect. The fix is small and isolated: wrap the `create` (and the batch loop) in a try/except IntegrityError and return 422 (or 409) with a "duplicate active rate card for this key" message — the endpoint already returns 422 for other validation failures, so the response contract is unchanged. Purely defensive, no migration, no SDK change. Worth doing immediately; it's a one-function patch with no blast radius.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** If a customer accidentally creates the same price card twice, UBB throws a server error (500) instead of a polite "that already exists." A 500 looks like the product is broken and erodes trust during evaluation. Turning it into a clear 4xx message is a tiny fix that makes UBB look professional.

- Ingestion caps: batch ≤100 events/call (422 above); caller cost fields capped at 999_999_999_999 micros (~$1M) per event; tags ≤50 keys, key regex `^[a-z][a-z0-9_]{1,63}$`, values ≤256 chars; `usage_metrics` values must be ≥0 — no negative/correction events; corrections only via the billing refund endpoint, which is wallet-side (ubb-platform/api/v1/schemas.py:30-31; ubb-platform/apps/metering/usage/services/usage_service.py:16,77-94).

  > **Verified —** True. Batch min 1 / max 100 (ubb-platform/api/v1/schemas.py:57, `Field(min_length=1, max_length=100)`); cost fields capped `le=999_999_999_999` (schemas.py:30-31); tags ≤50 keys, key regex `^[a-z][a-z0-9_]{1,63}$`, values ≤256 chars (ubb-platform/apps/metering/usage/services/usage_service.py:16,83-94); `usage_metrics` values must be ≥0 (schemas.py:35-44) so there are no negative/correction events — corrections go through the wallet-side refund path. All confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** The 100-event batch cap is squarely competitive on the low end but small on the high end: Metronome's /ingest also caps at 100 events/request (03 §1, "maxItems: 100"), while Orb allows 500/batch (03 §2) and Lago 100/batch (03 §3). So 100 is fine — matches Metronome, half of Orb. Negative/correction events ARE a real difference: Orb supports single-event amendment via PUT and timeframe backfills that mark originals archived (03 §2), i.e. mutable corrections, whereas UBB forbids negative usage and corrects only on the money side. That's a deliberate UBB design (immutable events, wallet-side refunds — see bullet 10) and defensible, but the batch ceiling and the no-negative rule should be documented as intentional. The only competitive nudge worth considering: raise the batch cap toward 500 (Orb parity) — trivial config change (schemas.py:57), additive, but validate downstream per-item commit cost first. Otherwise keep and document.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** UBB takes up to 100 usage events per call, the same as Metronome and half of Orb — fine. You can't send "negative" events to undo a charge; you fix mistakes through refunds on the money side instead, which is a deliberate, auditable design. The one easy win is bumping the batch size to match Orb's 500 for very chatty customers.

- Schema/DB mismatch: `request_id` accepts up to 500 chars in the API schema (ubb-platform/api/v1/schemas.py:27) but the column is varchar(255) (ubb-platform/apps/metering/usage/models.py:17) — a 256–500 char request_id fails at the DB layer.

  > **Verified —** True — a real bug. The API schema accepts `request_id: str = Field(min_length=1, max_length=500)` (ubb-platform/api/v1/schemas.py:27) but the column is `request_id = models.CharField(max_length=255)` (ubb-platform/apps/metering/usage/models.py:17). A 256-500 char request_id passes schema validation then fails at the DB write (Postgres rejects/truncates to varchar(255)), surfacing as a 500-class error, not a clean 422. Confirmed mismatch. (Note: `idempotency_key` is correctly 500 on both sides — schemas.py:28 / models.py:18 — so only request_id is wrong.)
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Comparable platforms bound their identifier fields consistently — Metronome's transaction_id is documented 1-128 chars and rejected cleanly out of range (03 §1); a schema/DB length disagreement that turns a long-but-valid id into a server error is a straightforward defect. The fix is a one-line decision: either lower the schema bound to `max_length=255` (cheapest, no migration) or widen the column to 500 via a migration to match idempotency_key. Recommend the schema change — 255 chars is ample for a request id and avoids a migration entirely. Effect: isolated, no SDK change, eliminates the 5xx. If the column is ever widened instead, it's a single additive migration with no data backfill.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** A customer can send a perfectly valid (just slightly long) request id and get a server error instead of a clear rejection — because two parts of UBB disagree on the maximum length. It's a one-line fix and removes a confusing crash.

- UsageEvents are immutable: no update, no delete; model `save()`/`delete()` raise (ubb-platform/apps/metering/usage/models.py:66-72). No void/adjust endpoint on the metering surface.

  > **Verified —** True. `UsageEvent.save()` raises "records are immutable and cannot be updated" on any non-insert, and `delete()` always raises (ubb-platform/apps/metering/usage/models.py:66-72). There is no update or void/adjust route on the metering surface (the only writers are POST /usage and /usage/batch; correction is wallet-side refund). Confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is where UBB diverges from the leaders, and it's a genuine, sourced gap. Orb explicitly supports audit-safe corrections: single-event amendment via PUT by event id (changing anything except timestamp/customer), timeframe backfills that mark originals "archived" (still queryable, excluded from billing), and event deprecation — "Orb never overwrites or permanently deletes ingested usage data" (03 §2, https://docs.withorb.com/guides/events-and-metrics/reporting-errors). Metronome voids and regenerates finalized invoices via /invoices/regenerate to absorb corrected usage (03 §1). UBB's hard immutability means the ONLY correction channel is a wallet refund, which doesn't fix the usage record, the margin attribution, or a postpaid line. The competitive fix preserves immutability but adds a correction primitive: a "reversal/amendment" event type that posts a NEW immutable row referencing the original (negative or replacement), so the ledger stays append-only AND corrections flow into margin and invoices. This is additive (a new event kind + a reference column + analytics that net reversals) but it touches the pricing provenance, margin queries, and postpaid aggregation — medium blast radius. Strongly worth doing: "I can never fix a mis-metered event" is a real objection in eval.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Once usage is recorded, UBB can never amend or reverse it on the usage side — your only recourse is a money refund, which doesn't correct the underlying record or your profit reporting. Competitors let you post an audit-safe correction. Adding a "reversal event" (a new entry that cancels an old one, without deleting history) closes a real objection buyers raise, because everyone eventually meters something wrong and needs to fix it cleanly.

- No GET `/usage/{event_id}`; the usage list omits tags, usage_metrics and pricing_provenance — full provenance is only available on the ingest response (ubb-platform/api/v1/metering_endpoints.py:237-254).

  > **Verified —** True. There is no `GET /usage/{event_id}` route in metering_endpoints.py — the only read is the cursor-paginated list `GET /customers/{customer_id}/usage` (ubb-platform/api/v1/metering_endpoints.py:208-254), whose response (lines 237-251) returns id, request_id, event_type, provider, costs, units, metadata, effective_at and OMITS tags, usage_metrics and pricing_provenance. Those rich fields appear only on the ingest response (schemas.py:79-83). Confirmed: full provenance is write-time-only and not re-retrievable.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Orb exposes events for read/amend by id (single-event PUT by event id implies addressable retrieval; events remain queryable after archival — 03 §2). Best practice for a UBB platform is that anything you ingested you can fetch back with its full pricing breakdown — provenance is the audit trail customers reconcile against. The fix is additive and cheap: add `GET /usage/{event_id}` returning the full UsageEvent including tags/usage_metrics/pricing_provenance (the data is already persisted on the row — models.py:32-34), and add those three fields to the list serializer (or a `?expand=provenance` flag to keep the list lean). No migration, no hot-path change, SDK gains one method. This materially improves debuggability and the reconciliation story.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Once UBB has priced an event, you can't ask it later "show me exactly how you priced this one" — the full breakdown is only returned at the moment you send it. Customers reconciling a bill need to look that up afterward. The data is already stored; UBB just needs a "fetch one event with its full math" endpoint.

- Backfill bounds: future skew 5 min; window default 34 days, hard max 60 (model clean), and `backfill_window_days` has NO public API writer — DB/ops change only. Months already claimed by a postpaid invoice are permanently closed to backfill (`billing_period_closed`) (ubb-platform/apps/platform/tenants/models.py:60-64,110-113; ubb-platform/apps/metering/usage/services/usage_service.py:31-74).

  > **Verified —** True. Future skew is 5 min (`_FUTURE_SKEW = timedelta(minutes=5)`, usage_service.py:19, enforced at :54); window defaults to 34 days (`backfill_window_days = PositiveIntegerField(default=34)`, tenants/models.py:64) and is read at usage_service.py:59-60; a closed postpaid month raises `billing_period_closed` (usage_service.py:69-74). `backfill_window_days` has NO public API writer — grep of api/v1/ for it returns zero matches. Confirmed (the "hard max 60" is enforced in the model's clean(), per doc).
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** UBB's 34-day window is deliberately aligned with the market: Metronome documents backdating "up to 34 days" (03 §1, identical number) and a 24h invoice grace period; Stripe meters accept timestamps "within the past 35 calendar days, max 5 minutes in the future" (03 §6 — UBB's 5-min future skew matches exactly); Orb reports "up to 12 hours after the timestamp" with a configurable grace (03 §2); Lago assigns by timestamp with a premium draft-invoice grace period (03 §3). So the bounds themselves are competitive and well-chosen. The one real gap is operability: the window has no self-serve control (DB/ops only) while Metronome/Orb expose grace configuration to the customer (Metronome via rep, Orb account-wide setting). Fix: add `backfill_window_days` to `TenantConfigIn` and the config PATCH endpoint (it's already a validated model field, clamped 0-60) — purely additive, one schema field + one assignment, SDK gains nothing structural. Keep the numeric bounds; just let tenants tune the window.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** UBB's rules for "how late can usage arrive" closely match Metronome and Stripe — that's good, not a weakness. The only catch is the customer can't adjust the window themselves; it takes an engineer changing the database. Exposing it as a normal setting is a quick win and removes a support ticket.

- Analytics: dimensions ≤6 per call; timeseries hourly window ≤92 days but ONLY enforced when both start_date and end_date are passed (an open-ended hourly query is unbounded, ubb-platform/api/v1/metering_endpoints.py:492); breakdowns are unpaginated full aggregates (no top-N parameter); inconsistent end_date semantics — `/analytics/usage` end_date is INCLUSIVE while `/analytics/usage/timeseries` end_date is EXCLUSIVE (ubb-platform/api/v1/metering_endpoints.py:351-354 vs ubb-platform/apps/metering/queries.py:257-259).

  > **Verified —** True, including the two quirks. The hourly-window cap is `if granularity == "hour" and start_date and end_date and (end_date - start_date).days > 92` (ubb-platform/api/v1/metering_endpoints.py:492) — so an open-ended hourly query (one or both dates omitted) bypasses the cap entirely and is unbounded. Breakdowns are full unpaginated aggregates (no top-N param, metering_endpoints.py:468-479). The end_date inconsistency is real: `/analytics/usage` uses `utc_next_day_start(end_date)` = INCLUSIVE (metering_endpoints.py:353-354), while `/analytics/usage/timeseries` uses `utc_day_start(end_date)` = EXCLUSIVE (ubb-platform/apps/metering/queries.py:258-259). Confirmed both bugs.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Orb publishes a dedicated Analytics component with 99.97% uptime and a separate Data Export surface (03 §2 status page); the leaders treat analytics as a hardened, bounded surface. No 03 fact prescribes a specific date-boundary convention, so I fall back to best practice: two sibling endpoints returning different results for the same `end_date` is a correctness defect that will produce mismatched dashboards, and an unbounded hourly scan is a denial-of-service/cost risk. Fixes are small and isolated: (1) make end_date semantics identical across both endpoints (recommend inclusive everywhere, change queries.py:259 to `utc_next_day_start`), (2) apply the 92-day hourly cap whenever granularity=hour regardless of whether dates are supplied (default the window if open-ended), and (3) add an optional `limit`/top-N to breakdowns. All additive/defensive, no migration, no SDK contract break beyond the date-semantics correction (which should be released as a documented fix). Worth doing — these are quiet correctness bugs.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Two of UBB's reports interpret the same "up to this date" differently, so a customer can pull the same range twice and get two different numbers — exactly the kind of thing that destroys trust in a billing tool. And one report can be asked to scan an unlimited amount of data, which is slow and costly. Both are small, contained fixes.

- Margin: trend periods clamp 1..36 monthly snapshots; `/margin/unprofitable` reads persisted monthly snapshots (not live); default windows are month-to-date; no SDK wrapper for `/margin/summary`, the `/margin` list, or `/margin/threshold`; the SDK `CustomerMargin` dataclass silently drops API fields (`revenue_mode`, `usage_revenue_micros`, `total_revenue_micros`, `event_count`) because of its field filter (ubb-sdk/ubb/metering.py:262-264; ubb-sdk/ubb/types.py:133-140).

  > **Verified —** True on all counts. Trend clamps `max(1, min(periods, 36))` (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/api/margin_endpoints.py:189); `/margin/unprofitable` reads persisted `CustomerEconomics` snapshots, not live (margin_endpoints.py:88-90); windows default month-to-date (`_window`, margin_endpoints.py:29-34). The endpoints `/margin/summary`, the `/margin` list, and `/margin/threshold` all exist server-side (margin_endpoints.py:37, 211, 98) but the SDK has NO wrapper for them (grep of ubb-sdk shows wrappers only for /margin/{id}, /by-dimension, /unprofitable, /{id}/trend, revenue, revenue-mode, business). And the SDK `CustomerMargin` dataclass drops API fields: `compute_live` returns revenue_mode/usage_revenue_micros/total_revenue_micros/event_count (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/economics/services.py:33-41) but the dataclass (ubb-sdk/ubb/types.py:134-140) lacks them and metering.py:263-264 filters the response to `__dataclass_fields__` — so they're silently discarded. Confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is a UBB-specific margin/COGS feature (the cost-card model is UBB's own), so 03 offers no direct competitor parallel — fall back to SDK best practice: an SDK that silently swallows fields the API returns is a footgun (a customer reading `total_revenue_micros` off the SDK gets nothing and assumes zero revenue). Two cheap, additive fixes: (1) add the four missing fields to the `CustomerMargin` dataclass (types.py) so the filter stops dropping them, and (2) add SDK wrappers for `get_margin_summary`, `list_margin`, and `get/set_margin_threshold` (one method each, mirroring existing ones). No server change, no migration; pure SDK additions. Worth doing — these are correctness/completeness gaps that make the margin product look thinner and buggier than it is.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** UBB's backend computes richer profit numbers (total revenue, per-customer event counts) than its official code library hands back — the library quietly throws those fields away, and a few profit reports have no library shortcut at all. So a customer using the SDK sees a smaller, buggier picture than the product actually offers. Filling in the SDK is quick and makes the margin feature look as complete as it really is.

- No streaming/websocket ingestion, no CSV/S3 bulk import, no event search by metadata/request_id, no export endpoint — retrieval is the cursor-paginated per-customer list plus aggregates (ubb-platform/api/v1/metering_endpoints.py:208-254,338-497).

  > **Verified —** True. Ingestion is HTTP POST /usage and /usage/batch only (no websocket/stream consumer in the codebase); retrieval is the cursor-paginated per-customer list (ubb-platform/api/v1/metering_endpoints.py:208-254) plus the analytics aggregates (:338-497). There is no export endpoint, no event search by metadata/request_id (the list only filters by tag_key+tag_value, metering_endpoints.py:218-219), and no CSV/S3 import path. Confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is a real scale/integration gap the leaders cover. Lago offers Kafka, Kinesis and S3 ingestion connectors (explicitly "not subject to REST API rate limits", 03 §3) and an S3/data-pipeline export on paid tiers; Orb advertises hosted streaming aggregation at "250,000+ events/second" and a dedicated Data Export component (03 §2); Metronome lists a Data Export surface on its status page and claims 100k events/sec (03 §1). UBB's per-call HTTP model is fine for moderate AI volumes (matches Metronome's 100/batch) but blocks high-throughput tenants and bulk migration off a competitor. The realistic, staged fix: (1) near-term, add an async CSV/S3 bulk-import job that fans rows into the existing `record_usage` choke point (additive, reuses all pricing/idempotency logic, one new Celery task + endpoint) and a paginated export/dump endpoint; (2) longer-term, a queue/stream connector (Kafka/Kinesis/SQS) feeding the same choke point — structurally larger because it introduces a new ingest path and backpressure handling, but it can still terminate at `record_usage` so pricing semantics are unchanged. Prioritise CSV/S3 import + export first (high deal value, low risk); defer streaming until a volume customer demands it.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** UBB only accepts usage one web request at a time and can't bulk-import a file or stream from a queue, and it can't export the raw data back out. That hurts two ways: very high-volume AI customers can't fire-hose events in, and a customer switching from a rival can't easily load their history or take their data with them. Adding file import/export first (the cheap, high-value part) removes the biggest onboarding and lock-in objections; true streaming can wait until a big customer needs it.


### 5.2 Money, wallets & spend control

- Recording usage is NEVER blocked by funds or suspension — `record_usage` has no status/balance check (ubb-platform/apps/metering/usage/services/usage_service.py:113-186); enforcement is only at `/pre-check` (advisory unless the integrator calls it), run hard-stops, and after-the-fact suspension. A customer who skips pre-check can overdraw without bound until suspension fires asynchronously.

  > **Verified —** True. `record_usage` (ubb-platform/apps/metering/usage/services/usage_service.py:113-221) does idempotency, effective_at validation, currency match, pricing, optional run accumulation, and the insert — there is no wallet-balance or `customer.status` read anywhere in the path. The only real-time spend stop is `RunService.accumulate_cost` (runs/services.py:81-100), which only fires when the caller passed a `run_id`. The balance gate lives in `RiskService.check` (gating/services/risk_service.py:44) but is reached only via POST `/pre-check`, which the integrator must call. Suspension is asynchronous, set later by the drawdown handler on overage (billing/handlers.py:85-87) or a failed Stripe invoice. So a caller who skips pre-check and runs can overdraw without bound until suspension fires on a later event. True.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is a deliberate "meter the truth, never lose an event" stance shared by the metering-first vendors: Metronome ingest is fire-and-forget with no synchronous balance gate (03 Metronome ingest, https://docs.metronome.com/api-reference/usage/ingest-events). The synchronous-enforcement model is OpenMeter's entitlements: "enforce usage quotas per feature with real-time balance tracking … and grace periods" (03 OpenMeter, https://github.com/openmeterio/openmeter), and Stripe's credit burndown. Fix without breaking ingest: keep recording unconditional, but add an opt-in synchronous gate flag (tenant `enforce_at_ingest`) that runs the existing `RiskService` balance/status check inside `record_usage` before the insert and raises a typed 402/429 — additive, reuses the gate, no migration beyond one bool. Cheaper: just make pre-check non-optional in the SDK facade and document it loudly.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Today a customer who forgets to call the pre-check can run up an unlimited bill before UBB notices and suspends them — fine for trusted enterprise contracts, dangerous for self-serve. Offering a one-flag "block at the door when out of funds" option turns UBB from after-the-fact alarm into real-time guardrail, which is what risk-averse buyers expect.

- No unsuspend/reactivate API exists anywhere (auditor grep for `status="active"`/reactivate across non-test code matches only referral programs); a suspended customer stays gated until someone edits the row manually — topping up does NOT clear suspension (`apply_topup_credit` never touches `customer.status`, ubb-platform/apps/billing/topups/services.py:61-109).

  > **Verified —** True. A repo grep for `reactivate`/`status="active"` writes finds only the referrals program (referrals/api/endpoints.py:145-156) — never a Customer. Customers are set `status="suspended"` in billing/handlers.py:86 (overage) and connectors/stripe/webhooks.py:226,329 (failed invoice), but nothing flips them back. `apply_topup_credit` (topups/services.py:61-109) credits the wallet and grant lot but never touches `customer.status`, so paying off the debt does not lift the gate. The drawdown re-suspend guard `owner.status == "active"` (handlers.py:85) also won't re-arm because nothing returns the row to active. True — recovery is a manual DB/admin row edit.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Best practice (no direct 03 fact on a reactivate endpoint per vendor): lifecycle state should be operator-controllable through the API, and dunning recovery should auto-reactivate on payment. Stripe's own model auto-resumes once an invoice is paid. Fix: add POST `/api/v1/billing/customers/{id}/reactivate` that sets `status="active"` (guarded so it cannot un-close a `closed` account) and emit a `customer.reactivated` event; additive, no migration. Higher-value: in `apply_topup_credit`, after a credit that lifts balance back above `-min_balance`, clear a `min_balance_exceeded` suspension and emit the event — closing the loop so a top-up self-heals. Leave Stripe-invoice-failure suspensions to clear on the paid webhook. The ripple is the outbox (one new event type) and the handler money path (one extra status write inside the existing savepoint).
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Right now, once a customer is cut off, the only way back is an engineer editing the database — and even paying their bill does not restore service. That is an operational landmine and a bad customer experience. A reactivate endpoint plus "top-up automatically un-suspends" makes recovery self-serve and instant.

- POST `/debit` has no balance floor and emits NO overage/suspend/balance-low events (ubb-platform/api/v1/billing_endpoints.py:54-91) — external debits can silently drive a wallet negative; `idempotency_key` is optional on debit/credit (None = retries double-apply).

  > **Verified —** True. `debit` (billing_endpoints.py:54-91) locks the wallet, unconditionally does `wallet.balance_micros -= amount`, writes a DEBIT row, allocates against grants — no floor check, no `min_balance`, and no `BalanceOverage`/`CustomerSuspended`/`BalanceLow` events (contrast the usage-drawdown path in handlers.py:80-100, which emits all three). So an external debit drives the wallet arbitrarily negative silently. `idempotency_key` is `Optional[...]=None` on both `DebitRequest` and `CreditRequest` (schemas.py:163,171); when None, the dedup lookup at debit:70 is skipped, so a retried debit double-applies. True on every point.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Orb and Metronome "strongly encourage" / treat idempotency keys as first-class on POST and replay safely within a 24-48h window (03 Orb idempotency, https://docs.withorb.com/api-reference/idempotency; 03 Metronome idempotency, https://docs.metronome.com/developer-resources/use-api/idempotency/). Best practice: balance mutations are never silently unguarded. Fix: (a) make `idempotency_key` required on `DebitRequest`/`CreditRequest` (schema-only change; SDK already passes none today so also wire it through — see 5.6) — or generate a server key; (b) factor the overage/suspend/balance-low emission block out of handlers.py:80-100 into a shared helper and call it from `debit` so external debits trip the same alarms; (c) optionally honor `min_balance` as a floor. Additive, no migration. Ripple: the SDK debit/credit (ubb-sdk/ubb/billing.py) must send the key, and the shared emit helper touches the outbox.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** The external-debit endpoint can quietly push a customer into the red with no warning fired, and if the call is retried it charges twice. Requiring an idempotency key and firing the same overage alarms the usage path already fires closes a real money-leak and double-charge risk.

- Hosted checkout and receipt invoices hardcode currency 'usd' regardless of the tenant's `default_currency` (ubb-platform/apps/billing/connectors/stripe/stripe_api.py:59; ubb-platform/apps/billing/connectors/stripe/receipts.py:64) even though wallets/grants carry the tenant currency — a non-USD tenant's top-up checkout would charge USD. Only 18 two-decimal currencies are supported tenant-wide; zero-decimal (jpy/krw) rejected (ubb-platform/apps/platform/tenants/models.py:12-20); one currency per tenant, no FX (ubb-platform/apps/metering/usage/services/usage_service.py:135-147).

  > **Verified —** True, and worse than the doc states. `create_checkout_session` hardcodes `"currency": "usd"` (connectors/stripe/stripe_api.py:59) AND `charge_saved_payment_method` hardcodes `currency="usd"` on the PaymentIntent (stripe_api.py:120) — so BOTH the hosted top-up and the auto-top-up off-session charge bill USD. `ReceiptService.create_topup_receipt` hardcodes `currency="usd"` on the invoice item (receipts.py:64). Meanwhile wallets are created in the tenant currency (locking.py:30-36) and usage is denominated in it (usage_service.py:139-147). A non-USD tenant's customer would be charged USD by Stripe but credited tenant-currency micros 1:1 — a real bug. `micros_to_cents` divides by 10_000 (stripe_service.py:27-37), correct only for 2-decimal currencies, which is exactly the set UBB allows (tenants/models.py:12-20). True.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Orb/Metronome push multi-currency invoices to Stripe carrying the correct currency (03 Orb Stripe sync, https://docs.withorb.com/integrations-and-exports/stripe). The precise fix: thread `customer.tenant.default_currency` into all three Stripe call sites — replace each literal `"usd"` with `(customer.tenant.default_currency or "usd").lower()` in `create_checkout_session`, `charge_saved_payment_method`, and `ReceiptService.create_topup_receipt`. Because UBB already rejects zero-decimal currencies (the `SUPPORTED_CURRENCIES` set in tenants/models.py is all 1/100-minor-unit), `micros_to_cents`'s `// 10_000` stays correct — no zero-decimal helper (the code's flagged "CUR-2") is needed for the supported set. No migration, no SDK change; blast radius is three lines plus the platform-fee invoice which also hardcodes usd (stripe/services/stripe_service.py:195, a sibling §5.5 item). Add a test per non-USD currency.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** A European tenant on EUR would have their customers' top-ups charged in dollars by Stripe while their wallet shows euros — a money-correctness bug that blocks selling outside the US. It is a three-line fix and should ship before any non-USD tenant goes live.

- Validation bounds: top-up/withdraw/grant/auto-top-up amounts must be cent-aligned (% 10_000 == 0); debit/credit/grant amounts capped at 999_999_999_999 micros (~$1M) per call; grant `expires_in_days` ≤ 3650; idempotency keys ≤ 400–500 chars; list limits clamped to 100 (ubb-platform/api/v1/schemas.py:108-199).

  > **Verified —** True. Cent-alignment (`% 10_000 == 0`) is enforced on `ConfigureAutoTopUpRequest.top_up_amount_micros` (schemas.py:113-118), `CreateTopUpRequest.amount_micros` (126-131), `WithdrawRequest.amount_micros` (145-150), and `CreateGrantRequest.amount_micros` (194-199). Debit/credit/grant amounts are capped `le=999_999_999_999` (~$1M) (schemas.py:161,168,181). Grant `expires_in_days` is `gt=0, le=3650` (183). Idempotency keys: grant `max_length=400` (184), withdraw/refund/debit/credit `max_length=500` (142,156,163,171). List limits clamp to 100 (e.g. get_transactions billing_endpoints.py:342). All confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** These are sensible, conservative input bounds, not a gap — keep them. The one nuance worth noting against competitors: cent-alignment on amounts is a corollary of the single-minor-unit (1/100) assumption that also drives the currency limitation; it is correct for the 18 supported 2-decimal currencies and would need revisiting only if zero-decimal currencies (jpy/krw) are ever added (the same "CUR-2" minor-unit helper called out in tenants/models.py:12-16). No code change recommended; document the $1M/event ceiling and cent-alignment in the public API reference so integrators don't discover them via 422s. No competitor 03 fact contradicts any bound (Orb caps event property integers at int64; Stripe meters cap dimension cardinality — different axes).
  >
  > **In plain terms —** These are guardrails, not limits that hurt — whole-cent amounts, a sane per-call dollar ceiling, and capped list sizes. Keep them; just publish them so a customer's engineers aren't surprised. The only forward-looking caveat is that the whole-cent rule is tied to UBB being a two-decimal-currency product.

- Usage refunds are whole-event only (no partial amount); a second refund of the same event under a new idempotency_key is allowed and lands entirely as base credit (`refunded_micros` caps only the LOT re-fund, not the wallet credit) (ubb-platform/api/v1/billing_endpoints.py:268-335).

  > **Verified —** True. `refund_usage` (billing_endpoints.py:268-335) takes only `usage_event_id` + `idempotency_key` (RefundRequest, schemas.py:153-156) — no amount field — and credits the full `get_usage_event_cost(...)` (302). A second refund under a NEW idempotency_key passes the dedup check (291-294 keys on idempotency_key, not event), credits the full cost again to the wallet (302), then calls `GrantLedger.refund` on the original deduction; `refunded_micros` caps only the re-fund back into LOTS (grants.py:273), so the second time the lots are already maxed and the entire credit lands as base. The endpoint comment at 316-318 says exactly this. True.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Orb's correction model is amendment/backfill at the event level with full audit safety ("never overwrites or permanently deletes"; PUT single-event amend) rather than a money-refund of a wallet (03 Orb reporting-errors, https://docs.withorb.com/guides/events-and-metrics/reporting-errors). Best practice: a refund must be idempotent on the underlying charge, not just the request key. Fix: (a) add an optional `amount_micros` to RefundRequest for partial refunds, validated `<= cost`; (b) track cumulative refunded-to-wallet per usage_event (a column or a sum over REFUND txns referencing the event) and reject/clamp once `refunded >= cost`, so a second full refund cannot double-credit. Small migration (one indexed column or a query) plus endpoint logic; the outbox `refund.requested` event is unchanged. Ripple: the lot-aware `GrantLedger.refund` already caps correctly — only the wallet-credit leg needs the cap.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** A support agent can refund the same charge twice (under two ticket IDs) and the customer keeps double the money — and there is no way to refund just part of a charge. Capping total refund at the original amount and allowing partial refunds removes a money-leak and matches how finance teams actually issue credits.

- Expired/voided grant lots are never re-inflated by refunds (their share lands as base, ubb-platform/apps/billing/wallets/grants.py:281-284); grant expiry/void debits are clamped to never push the balance below zero, so an overdrawn wallet can "keep" expired credit it already spent (grants.py:82-83; ubb-platform/api/v1/billing_endpoints.py:535).

  > **Verified —** True. `GrantLedger.refund` only restores slices into still-active lots; its docstring (grants.py:281-284) states expired/voided lots are NOT re-funded — "their unspent remainder was already destroyed … re-inflating them would double-create money," so that share lands as base. The expiry debit clamps `debit = min(remaining, max(balance, 0))` (grants.py:83) and void clamps the same way (billing_endpoints.py:535), so an overdrawn wallet's expiry/void debits stop at zero — meaning credit already spent into the red is never clawed back, i.e. the wallet effectively "keeps" expired credit it already used. True; this is the documented G1/G3 conservation design.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Stripe Credit Grants model explicit states pending/granted/depleted/expired/voided with priority-ordered application and expiry only when `expires_at` set (03 Stripe credits, https://docs.stripe.com/billing/subscriptions/usage-based/billing-credits) — expired credit is simply gone, not re-inflated; UBB's behavior matches that principle. This is deliberate and correct: re-inflating a destroyed lot would mint money, and clamping at zero avoids charging a customer for promo credit they were given. Recommendation: KEEP as-is and document the invariant in the public grants docs (the G1 conservation rule: `sum(remaining of active lots) <= max(balance,0)`), so tenants understand that a refund of a charge originally funded by since-expired promo credit returns as spendable base cash, and that going negative does not retroactively reclaim already-spent expiring credit. No code change.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** This is correct accounting, not a bug: once promo credit expires it's gone, and UBB will never secretly recreate it or claw back credit a customer already spent. The only thing to do is explain it clearly so finance understands why a refund sometimes comes back as cash rather than restored promo.

- Promo credit is not withdrawable (withdraw availability = balance − active promo remaining, ubb-platform/api/v1/billing_endpoints.py:225) but IS spendable by `/debit` and usage; `/credit` never creates a lot (base money only).

  > **Verified —** True. `withdraw` computes availability as `wallet.balance_micros - GrantLedger.promo_remaining(wallet)` and rejects if that is below the requested amount (billing_endpoints.py:225); the allocation excludes promo (`exclude_promo=True`, 241-242). Yet promo IS spendable: the usage drawdown (handlers.py:78 `GrantLedger.allocate`) and `/debit` (billing_endpoints.py:89) allocate without excluding promo. `/credit` creates an ADJUSTMENT WalletTransaction only (billing_endpoints.py:124-132) and never a CreditGrant lot — its docstring says base grows directly (96-101). All three sub-claims true.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This mirrors Stripe's promotional-vs-paid credit distinction and grant categories (03 Stripe credits, https://docs.stripe.com/billing/subscriptions/usage-based/billing-credits): promotional credit is consumable but not cash-out-able. Deliberate and correct — keep it. The one honest gap is discoverability: `/credit` silently meaning "non-expiring base cash, no lot" is a footgun, because a tenant reaching for "give this customer $50" might use `/credit` (base, withdrawable) when they meant a promo grant (not withdrawable). Recommendation: KEEP the promo-exclusion rule and document it in the withdraw API ("withdrawable = balance − active promo"), and steer tenants to POST `/grants` (kind=promo|paid) for anything with expiry/withdrawal semantics, reserving `/credit` for plain base adjustments. No code change; possibly a docstring/reference note and an SDK helper naming nudge.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Free promotional credit can be spent on usage but not cashed out — exactly right, so customers can't convert a marketing giveaway into a payout. The only improvement is clearer docs so a tenant knows the difference between "give base cash" and "give promo credit," because the two endpoints behave very differently.

- Per-customer `min_balance`, `topup_grant_expiry_days`, `RiskConfig` rate limits/`gate_fail_closed`, and `BillingTenantConfig` run_cost_limit/hard_stop_balance/min_balance have NO API or admin surface on this branch — ORM-only (auditor grep of `api/` shows zero references; ubb-platform/apps/billing/wallets/admin.py registers only Wallet + WalletTransaction, omitting CustomerBillingProfile).

  > **Verified —** True. `min_balance` is read from `CustomerBillingProfile.min_balance_micros` / `BillingTenantConfig.min_balance_micros` (queries.py:28-40) with no API writer. `topup_grant_expiry_days` is read from `CustomerBillingProfile` (grants.py:358-371), no writer. `RiskConfig` (max_requests_per_minute, gate_fail_closed) is read in risk_service.py:18-33, no writer. `BillingTenantConfig.run_cost_limit_micros`/`hard_stop_balance_micros`/`min_balance_micros` are read at run creation (risk_service.py:61-67) and have no public PATCH (the doc's §5.5 confirms TenantConfigIn omits them). `wallets/admin.py` registers only Wallet + WalletTransaction — CustomerBillingProfile, RiskConfig, BillingTenantConfig are absent. True; these are ORM/DB-only on this branch.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Competitors expose risk/limit configuration through their app or API (Orb/Metronome configure alerts, credit thresholds, and limits via API/dashboard; 03 Orb/Metronome). Some of these are intentionally operator-only (e.g. platform-side risk), but `min_balance` (allowed overdraft), `topup_grant_expiry_days`, and per-customer budget knobs are tenant-facing money policy and should be self-serve. Fix: add a `CustomerBillingProfile` writer — PUT `/api/v1/billing/customers/{id}/profile` accepting `min_balance_micros`, `topup_grant_expiry_days` — and surface `run_cost_limit_micros`/`hard_stop_balance_micros`/tenant `min_balance` on the tenant-config PATCH; register the models in admin as an immediate operator stopgap. Additive (the fields exist; no migration), one new schema + endpoint + SDK method. `RiskConfig.gate_fail_closed` can stay operator-only but should at least be admin-registered.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Several real money dials — how far a customer may go negative, when their paid credit expires, per-customer spend ceilings — can only be set by an engineer in the database today. Exposing them as normal settings removes a support bottleneck and lets customers self-configure their risk posture, which is table stakes for the competitors.

- Run balance floor uses the pre-check balance SNAPSHOT minus run-local cost — concurrent spend from other runs/seats is invisible to it (ubb-platform/apps/platform/runs/models.py:37-41; ubb-platform/apps/platform/runs/services.py:82); a batch kill failure leaves the run active with only a log (ubb-platform/api/v1/metering_endpoints.py:160-166).

  > **Verified —** True. `create_run` stores `balance_snapshot_micros` captured at pre-check (risk_service.py:62-67 passes the balance read at :38) and the model comment says it's frozen at creation (runs/models.py:37-41). `accumulate_cost` computes `estimated_balance = balance_snapshot_micros - new_total` (runs/services.py:82) — purely the snapshot minus this run's own accumulated cost; concurrent spend from other runs or sibling seats on the same pooled wallet is invisible to it. The batch-kill failure leaving the run active with only a log is at metering_endpoints.py:160-166. True.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** The metering-first vendors enforce real-time spend against a live aggregated balance / credit burndown (Stripe "real-time credit burndown," 03 Stripe advanced UBB, https://docs.stripe.com/billing/subscriptions/usage-based/advanced/compare; OpenMeter "real-time balance tracking," 03 OpenMeter). UBB's snapshot is a deliberate isolation choice (a run's limit shouldn't shift mid-flight) but it means the per-run wallet floor is approximate under concurrency. Fix options, ascending cost: (a) document it as a per-run soft floor, not a global guarantee — the real overdraft backstop is the post-drawdown suspension in handlers.py; (b) on each `accumulate_cost`, re-read the live owner wallet balance (one extra locked read) and floor against the lesser of snapshot-derived and live — more correct, small perf cost; (c) make the batch-kill failure raise a monitored alert rather than only logging. (a)+(c) are cheap and honest; (b) is the real fix if hard real-time per-run floors matter. No migration.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** A run's "stop at this balance" guard is measured against a photo of the wallet taken when the run started, so two runs spending at once can each think there's money left and jointly overshoot. The reliable safety net is the after-the-fact suspension; if customers need hard real-time per-run floors, UBB should check the live balance, and the rare "couldn't stop the run" case should page someone, not just log.

- Runs: no public endpoints to create (only billing pre-check with the `billing` product), kill, list, or GET a run — the only reads are the pre-check response and close_run's summary; run cost ceiling/wallet floor have no public API writer (auditor grep of `api/` matches tests only). Run accumulation counts BILLED cost, not provider cost (ubb-platform/apps/platform/runs/services.py:81).

  > **Verified —** True. Runs are created only as a side effect of POST `/pre-check` with `start_run=true` (risk_service.py:57-71), which requires the `billing` product (`_product_check`). There is no public create/kill/list/GET run endpoint — a repo grep matches only tests; the only run reads are the pre-check response (`run_id`, limits) and close_run's summary. `cost_limit_micros`/`hard_stop_balance_micros` come from `BillingTenantConfig` with no API writer (confirmed above). Run accumulation counts BILLED cost: `record_usage` calls `accumulate_cost(run_id, billed_cost_micros, ...)` (usage_service.py:170-172) and the run sums that (runs/services.py:81), not provider cost. All true.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** No direct 03 competitor fact on a "run/session" primitive — runs are a UBB-specific abstraction for agent executions, so this is greenfield rather than catch-up. Best practice for a first-class resource is full CRUD + read. Fix (additive, no migration): expose GET `/api/v1/billing/runs/{id}` and a cursor-paginated list (the model and `RunService` reads already exist), and a POST `.../runs/{id}/kill` wrapping `RunService.kill_run`; optionally a direct create decoupled from pre-check. Surface the run ceiling/floor via the tenant-config writer proposed in the ORM-only item. Note the billed-vs-provider-cost choice is deliberate and correct (the floor protects the customer's wallet, which is charged the billed amount) — document it. Ripple: new read endpoints + SDK wrappers; the §5.6 SDK gap (no run wrappers) would be closed in the same pass.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Runs (an agent execution UBB can cap and hard-stop) can be started and limited but not listed, fetched, or cancelled through the API, and their limits are DB-only. Giving runs proper read/kill endpoints turns a hidden internal mechanism into a feature customers can build dashboards and kill-switches on.

- Hard-stop is per-run only — there is no per-customer or per-tenant real-time spend ceiling on this surface (budget caps are enforced at pre-check time, default advisory).

  > **Verified —** True. The only synchronous, request-time hard ceiling is `RunService.accumulate_cost`'s two checks — per-run cost limit and per-run wallet floor (runs/services.py:84-100) — and they only engage when a `run_id` is supplied. Budget caps are evaluated in `BudgetService.check` reached via `RiskService.check` at `/pre-check` time only (risk_service.py:47-52), default `enforce_mode="advisory"` (so they alert, don't block) and are skipped entirely if pre-check isn't called. There is no per-customer or per-tenant real-time spend ceiling enforced at the ingest choke point. True.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Stripe describes real-time credit burndown with automatic top-ups and flat-fee-plus-overage as native advanced-UBB capabilities (03 Stripe advanced UBB, https://docs.stripe.com/billing/subscriptions/usage-based/advanced/compare); OpenMeter offers per-feature real-time quotas (03 OpenMeter). UBB's enforcement is post-hoc (drawdown → suspend) plus opt-in pre-check. Fix dovetails with the first §5.2 item: add an opt-in synchronous gate inside `record_usage` that consults the existing `BudgetService` and balance check before insert, so an enforcing budget cap or a depleted wallet blocks at ingest, not only at a pre-check the integrator may skip. Make `enforce_mode` default to enforcing for new prepaid customers, or at least surface a loud "your spend control is advisory only" warning. Additive (reuses BudgetService/RiskService), no migration; ripple is the ingest path and one config default.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** The only thing that can stop spend in real time is a per-run limit, and only if the integrator opted into runs; the per-customer budget "cap" merely warns by default. To a buyer who hears "spend control," that is weaker than it sounds — wiring the existing budget engine into the ingest path (and defaulting caps to actually-enforcing) delivers the real-time ceiling they expect.

- Budget caps: `cap_micros <= 0` disables the cap; enforcement is calendar-month UTC only (no custom periods despite the model's `period` field); the live counter skips backdated prior-month events — enforcing caps are evadable within `Tenant.backfill_window_days` (documented bypass, ubb-platform/apps/billing/gating/services/budget_service.py:136-142); threshold alerts dedup via OutboxEvent query, not a constraint (a rare duplicate is possible under concurrency, budget_service.py:100-111).

  > **Verified —** True. `BudgetService.check` returns allowed when `cfg is None or cap_micros <= 0` (budget_service.py:70). The period is always the current calendar month UTC via `_period()` (budget_service.py:13-21) regardless of the model's `period` field. The live counter (`record_usage_spend` → `record_spend`) is current-wall-clock-month only and the handler skips backdated prior-month events, with the docstring explicitly naming the bypass: "an enforcing-capped seat can backdate into the PRIOR month to evade the live cap — bounded by Tenant.backfill_window_days (0 = no backfill = airtight)" (budget_service.py:135-142). Threshold-alert dedup is an OutboxEvent `.exists()` query, not a DB constraint (budget_service.py:100-106), so a rare concurrent double-send is possible. All sub-claims true.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Competitors anchor usage to event timestamp and assign late events to the correct historical period (03 Lago ingesting-usage, https://getlago.com/docs/guide/events/ingesting-usage; 03 Orb backfill). UBB's effective-month truth is the same idea; the live Redis cap is just a fast advisory mirror, with the hourly Postgres rebuild (`reconcile_customer`, effective_at-filtered) as source of truth. The backdating bypass is real but bounded and documented. Fixes: (a) for the dedup race, add a unique constraint on (event_type, tenant, customer_id, period, level) so a duplicate threshold alert is impossible, not just unlikely — small migration; (b) support the model's `period` field (custom/anniversary windows) if customers ask, otherwise drop the dead field; (c) document that enforcing caps are evadable within the backfill window and that setting `backfill_window_days=0` makes them airtight. Cheap, mostly hardening; the backdating tradeoff is inherent to honoring late events.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Budget caps work on a calendar-month basis and a clever customer can dodge an enforcing cap by backdating usage into last month — bounded by how far back you allow backdating, and zero backdating closes it entirely. Add a database guard so duplicate "you hit 80%" alerts can't slip out, and tell customers the one knob that makes caps truly tamper-proof.

- `reconcile_wallet_balances` is detect-only (logs drift, never repairs) (ubb-platform/apps/billing/wallets/tasks.py:10-96); drawdown self-repair covers prepaid tenants only and a 7-day arrival window (tasks.py:126-127); the Stripe top-up sweep covers 4 days and only PIs carrying `metadata.topup_attempt_id` (ubb-platform/apps/billing/connectors/stripe/tasks.py:127-153).

  > **Verified —** True. `reconcile_wallet_balances` (wallets/tasks.py:10-96) logs `error` on cached-vs-ledger drift, grant-overshoot, and per-grant conservation breaks but writes no correcting row — pure detection. `reconcile_usage_drawdowns` (tasks.py:104-135) iterates only `billing_mode="prepaid"` tenants with `LOOKBACK = timedelta(days=7)` (tasks.py:100). The Stripe top-up sweep (`reconcile_topups_with_stripe`, connectors/stripe/tasks.py:127-153) uses a 4-day `created` cutoff (127) and only acts on PIs whose `metadata.topup_attempt_id` is set (152). All true.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Orb publishes per-component uptime and frames "idempotency guarantees to ensure your data is complete and correct" (03 Orb status/pricing, https://status.withorb.com); correctness is treated as a guarantee, not a log line. Detect-only on the wallet-vs-ledger check is partly deliberate (auto-repairing the cached balance from the ledger is safe and arguably should be done; auto-repairing the harder grant-conservation invariants is risky and should alert a human). Fix: (a) make `reconcile_wallet_balances` REPAIR the cached `balance_micros` from the authoritative `Sum(amount_micros)` ledger when they diverge (the ledger is the source of truth) while keeping grant-invariant violations alert-only — small, additive; (b) ensure the drift log is wired to an actual alert/pager, not just stderr; (c) document the drawdown 7-day / Stripe 4-day windows as the bounded self-heal horizons (both deliberately exceed the respective retry horizons). The risk in (a) is masking a real bug, so log loudly even when repairing.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** UBB notices when a wallet's balance and its transaction history disagree but does nothing to fix it — it just writes a log nobody may read. Since the transaction ledger is the source of truth, UBB should auto-correct the cached balance from it (and alert a human for the trickier credit-lot mismatches), so a glitch self-heals instead of festering.

- Rate limiting is per-seat fixed-window in Redis and silently disabled when Redis is down; there is no fail-closed option for it or for the wallet-balance gate (ubb-platform/apps/billing/gating/services/risk_service.py:22-33).

  > **Verified —** True. `RiskService.check` rate-limits on `cache_key = f"ratelimit:{customer.id}:rpm"` — per-seat (the addressed customer, not the owner) — using a fixed 60s window (`cache.set(..., timeout=60)`, risk_service.py:24-31). The whole block is wrapped in `try/except Exception: pass` (risk_service.py:32-33), so any Redis failure silently disables rate limiting (fail-open) with no opt-out. The balance gate (risk_service.py:44) likewise has no fail-closed switch (only the budget gate honors `fail_closed`/`gate_fail_closed`). True.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Vendors publish concrete ingest rate limits and 429 semantics — Lago 500 req/s per org with `x-ratelimit-*` headers (03 Lago, https://getlago.com/docs/guide/events/ingesting-usage), Stripe 1,000 calls/s on v1 meter events (03 Stripe meters, https://docs.stripe.com/billing/subscriptions/usage-based/recording-usage-api), Orb 10 req/s test mode (03 Orb). None publish their fail-open/closed posture; fail-open during a cache outage is a common availability choice. Fixes: (a) add a `RiskConfig.rate_limit_fail_closed` (and a balance-gate fail-closed) so security-sensitive tenants can opt into deny-on-Redis-down — additive bool, no behavior change by default; (b) consider sliding-window or token-bucket if burst fairness matters (fixed-window allows 2x bursts at the boundary); (c) emit a metric when the rate-limit path swallows a cache error so the outage is visible. Low cost, mostly config + observability. The per-seat (not pooled-owner) keying is arguably correct since rate-limit is a control concern that stays per-seat (consistent with the §5.2 routing model).
  >
  > **In plain terms —** If Redis hiccups, UBB stops rate-limiting entirely and lets all traffic through, with no way to tell it "block instead" — fine for uptime, risky for abuse-sensitive customers. Add an opt-in "fail closed" switch and an alert when the limiter goes dark, so cautious customers can choose safety over availability.

- Top-up, debit, credit, withdraw, refund and auto-top-up act on the ADDRESSED customer's own wallet — they do not resolve the pooled billing owner (only grants, pre-check, and the usage drawdown/repair do); a pooled seat addressed directly gets its own (normally empty) wallet (ubb-platform/api/v1/billing_endpoints.py:54-335 vs :437).

  > **Verified —** True. `debit` (billing_endpoints.py:67), `credit` (:112), `withdraw` (:215), `refund_usage` (:286) all call `lock_for_billing(customer.id)` on the ADDRESSED customer; `lock_for_billing` (locking.py:15-40) creates/locks that customer's OWN wallet with no owner resolution. Auto-top-up's `apply_topup_credit` (topups/services.py:82) locks `attempt.customer_id` directly. By contrast grants (billing_endpoints.py:437,485,525), `RiskService.check` (risk_service.py:9-10 via `resolve_billing_owner`), and the usage drawdown/repair (handlers.py:46-50; wallets/tasks.py:128-132) DO resolve the pooled billing owner. So a pooled seat addressed directly by /debit etc. transacts against its own (normally empty) wallet, diverging from where usage actually draws. True.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** No direct 03 fact (pooled-seat money topology is a UBB-specific model). Best practice: one consistent answer to "whose money is this?" The split is almost certainly an oversight, not design — the resolver exists and the money-truth paths (drawdown, pre-check, grants) already use it, so the wallet-mutation endpoints should too. Fix: route `debit`/`credit`/`withdraw`/`refund` and `apply_topup_credit` through `customer.resolve_billing_owner()` before `lock_for_billing`, exactly as grants do at billing_endpoints.py:437. Additive, no migration. Ripple: must be deliberate per verb — for a pooled topology, top-up/debit/credit/withdraw should hit the business wallet (matching where usage drains); for an allocated topology the seat funds itself so the seat wallet is correct (resolve_billing_owner already returns self there). Add tests for pooled-seat /debit and /top-up landing on the business wallet. This also de-risks the "empty seat wallet silently accepting money" footgun.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** For a company whose team shares one pooled balance, paying or refunding an individual seat directly hits a separate empty sub-wallet instead of the shared company wallet that usage actually drains — so money can land in the wrong place. The fix is to make every money endpoint ask the same "who pays?" question the usage path already asks.

- Withdrawals never move real money — no Stripe payout integration; the platform writes the ledger row and emits `billing.withdrawal_requested`; the payout is the tenant's job (ubb-platform/api/v1/billing_endpoints.py:201-252).

  > **Verified —** True. `withdraw` (billing_endpoints.py:201-252) checks balance minus promo, decrements the wallet, writes a WITHDRAWAL ledger row and grant allocation, and emits a `billing.withdrawal_requested` outbox event — there is no Stripe payout/transfer call anywhere in the path. The actual disbursement is left to the tenant's own systems reacting to the event. True; this is a deliberate boundary.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** UBB intentionally lets the tenant's Stripe Connect account own payment movement: customer-facing charges go through the connected account (stripe_api.py) and payouts are Stripe's job, not UBB's. The competitors similarly defer settlement to Stripe Invoicing/payouts rather than moving money themselves (03 Orb Stripe sync, https://docs.withorb.com/integrations-and-exports/stripe; 03 Metronome Stripe, https://docs.metronome.com/integrations/invoice-integrations/stripe). Recommendation: KEEP this as a deliberate design — UBB is a ledger/billing engine, not a money-transmitter, and emitting an event keeps it out of payout-licensing/regulatory scope. But make it honest and safe: (a) document plainly that a withdrawal only debits the ledger and emits an event, the tenant must execute the payout (the §5.6 SDK footgun where `UBBClient.withdraw` delegates to `/debit` and skips even this event must be fixed separately); (b) optionally offer a thin Stripe `Transfer`/payout connector behind a flag for tenants who want UBB to drive it. No migration for keep-as-is.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** When a customer "withdraws," UBB only adjusts the books and tells the tenant to actually send the money — it deliberately doesn't touch real funds, which keeps UBB out of money-transmitter regulation. That's a sound boundary; just make sure it's clearly documented (and that the SDK's withdraw shortcut isn't quietly skipping even the notification).


### 5.3 Subscriptions & postpaid

- Trials and coupons DO NOT EXIST on this surface — an explicit non-goal; Stripe's own trial_period_days/Coupons on the connected account are the levers, UBB does not wrap or sync them (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/orchestration/service.py:248-252; ubb-platform/api/v1/platform_endpoints.py docstrings 147-148,216-217,229-230,241-242).

  > **Verified — True.** orchestration/service.py:248-252 carries the explicit "Trials and coupons are deliberate NON-goals" note, and the four lifecycle/plan docstrings at platform_endpoints.py (147-148, 216-217, 229-230, 241-242) repeat it. No `trial_period_days`, `coupon`, `discount`, or `promotion_code` argument is passed to any `Subscription.create`/`modify` (service.py:192-204); `PlanIn`/`SubscribeIn` (schemas.py:399-431) have no trial/coupon fields. Confirmed: this surface neither wraps nor syncs trials/coupons.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** All three competitors lean on Stripe for collection rather than reinventing discounts: Orb maps every item to Stripe products and lets Stripe collect (03 Orb, withorb.com/integrations/stripe); Metronome creates Stripe invoices on finalize (03 Metronome, docs.metronome.com/.../stripe); Stripe's own rate-card guidance says "use rate cards only for pure usage-based pricing without discounts or trials" (03 Stripe rate cards). So the *evidence* is that trials/coupons live in the subscription/invoice layer, which here is Stripe's connected account. This is a genuine non-goal, not a gap: the tenant configures `trial_period_days` and Coupons directly in their own Stripe and UBB rides whatever subscription results. The only honest caveat is discoverability — because UBB never reads back trial/discount state (see the sync bullet), a UBB-issued usage invoice consolidated onto a trialing/discounted renewal won't reflect that locally. Recommended posture: keep it a non-goal; optionally store a read-only `discount`/`trial_end` snapshot off the `customer.subscription.updated` webhook so margin/AR reporting isn't blind to Stripe-side promos.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** We deliberately don't build our own free-trials or discount-codes; the customer's own Stripe already does that better and we let it. The only thing worth adding later is *reading* those Stripe discounts back so our revenue reports aren't surprised by them.

- Plan `interval` is unvalidated: `PlanIn` accepts any string (ubb-platform/api/v1/schemas.py:399-405); the model column is max_length=5 (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/models.py:90), so a >5-char value (e.g. 'quarter') fails at the DB layer while 'week'/'day' would flow through to Stripe; `_INTERVAL_MONTHS` only maps month/year and the period fallback silently treats unknown intervals as 1 month (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/orchestration/service.py:52,74-80).

  > **Verified — True.** `PlanIn.interval` is a bare `str = "month"` with no validator (schemas.py:399-405); the model column is `max_length=5` (models.py:90), so 'quarter' (7 chars) raises at the DB layer while 'week'/'day' (<=5) persist and flow straight into `recurring={"interval": plan.interval}` on `Price.create` (service.py:137). `_INTERVAL_MONTHS = {"month": 1, "year": 12}` (service.py:52) and `_period_fallback_end` silently treats any unknown interval as 1 month (service.py:74-80). Confirmed real footgun on all three checks.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is a plain correctness gap, not a competitive feature — best practice is to reject invalid enums at the edge (Stripe's own meter/price APIs reject unknown enum values with 400). The fix is the cheapest real win in this section: add `Literal["month","year"]` (or an explicit allow-list validator) to `PlanIn.interval` and reuse it in `PlanUpdateIn` (today PATCH can't change interval at all — see the plan-CRUD bullet). Ripple is tiny and contained: one schema edit in schemas.py; no migration needed because the column already accepts both valid values; `_INTERVAL_MONTHS` already covers exactly the validated set so the fallback becomes unreachable for valid input; no SDK change beyond a docstring. If 'week'/'day' billing is ever genuinely wanted, that's a separate scoped feature (widen the column + extend `_INTERVAL_MONTHS` + period math), but it should be an opt-in, never an accidental pass-through. Recommend: validate now.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Right now a typo or odd value in a plan's billing interval either crashes deep in the database or quietly bills monthly when you asked for something else. Locking the field to the two intervals we actually support is a one-line, do-it-now fix.

- Single currency per tenant, no multi-currency/FX; only 2-decimal currencies; currency permanently locked once money exists; the provisioned Price currency is NOT stored locally so it can never be cross-checked later (ubb-platform/api/v1/tenant_endpoints.py:339-407; ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/orchestration/service.py:165-177).

  > **Verified — True.** `_currency_locked_reason` (tenant_endpoints.py:339-371) pins `default_currency` forever once ANY of five money objects exists, and the PATCH returns 409 `currency_locked` (379-407); only 2-decimal currencies pass `SUPPORTED_CURRENCIES`. service.py:165-177 confirms the provisioned Price currency is NOT stored locally (comment: "We do not store the provisioned price currency on the plan… a full cross-check… is deferred"), so a later mismatch can't be detected. Confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** I cannot assert competitor multi-currency support: 03 does not record multi-currency/FX facts for Metronome, Orb, or Lago, and the "could not verify" section forbids asserting anything beyond it. So this rests on best practice only: per-tenant single-currency with an immutable-once-money-exists rule is a sound, conservative design — it eliminates an entire class of FX/rounding bugs and matches the doc's stated intent. The genuine improvement is not "add FX" (a large program: per-currency wallets, price sets, invoice denomination, rate-card pinning) but closing the one honest weakness the code itself flags: store the provisioned Price currency on `TenantBillingPlan` (one nullable column + migration) so the lock can be *verified* rather than merely *assumed*. That's a small hardening with no SDK or webhook ripple. Full multi-currency should remain a deliberate non-goal until there's demand, and be scoped as its own program if so.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Each customer-platform picks one currency and we freeze it the moment real money moves — that's intentional and keeps us out of exchange-rate bug territory. The only cleanup worth doing is recording which currency we set in Stripe so we can prove the lock held, rather than trusting it.

- Billing cycle anchor is hard-coded to 00:00 UTC on the 1st of next month with create_prorations — no custom anchors, no anniversary billing, no proration_behavior choice at subscribe (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/orchestration/service.py:65-71,200-201).

  > **Verified — True.** `_next_month_anchor()` (service.py:65-71) returns 00:00 UTC on the 1st of next month, passed verbatim as `billing_cycle_anchor` with `proration_behavior="create_prorations"` on `Subscription.create` (service.py:200-201). No anchor or proration argument is exposed in `SubscribeIn` (schemas.py:429-431) or the subscribe endpoint (platform_endpoints.py:247-279). Confirmed: no custom anchors, no anniversary billing, no per-subscribe proration choice.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** 03 does not record competitor billing-anchor/anniversary facts, so I won't assert them. Best practice (and Stripe's native capability, which UBB is calling) is to support both calendar-aligned and anniversary anchors plus a `proration_behavior` choice — Stripe `Subscription.create` already accepts `billing_cycle_anchor` and `proration_behavior` directly, so the platform isn't the limiter, UBB's hard-coding is. This is a moderate, real feature for any tenant whose customers expect "bill me on my signup date." The fix: add optional `billing_cycle_anchor` (or an `anchor_mode` enum: `calendar`|`anniversary`) and `proration_behavior` to `SubscribeIn`, thread them through `subscribe()` (service.py:192-204). Ripple is modest: the postpaid close still assumes prior-calendar-month (tasks.py:64-93) and the consolidation window keys off the renewal draft (postpaid_service.py:458-491), so anniversary anchors would need the postpaid period math to follow the subscription period rather than the calendar month — that coupling makes it a scoped feature, not a one-liner. Recommend: ship calendar-vs-anniversary as a real roadmap item; it's a common deal-blocker.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Today every subscription bills on the 1st of the month, period. Customers who expect to be billed on their own signup anniversary can't be — adding that is a real, worthwhile feature, but it touches how usage invoices line up too, so it's a project, not a quick toggle.

- Lifecycle verbs only target "the latest non-canceled subscription of the billing owner" — no subscription-id addressing, no multi-subscription management, no plan upgrade/downgrade verb (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/orchestration/service.py:475-486). `cancel(at_period_end=false)` is irreversible here: `resume()` only clears a PENDING cancel/pause. The orchestrator's exhaustive verb list is ensure_plan_provisioned/subscribe/set_seats/cancel/pause/resume/update_plan_prices — nothing else.

  > **Verified — True.** `_find_active_mirror` (service.py:475-486) returns `StripeSubscription.objects.filter(customer=owner).exclude(status="canceled").order_by("-created_at").first()` — latest non-canceled of the billing owner, no sub-id parameter. cancel/pause/resume all call it; `resume()` (326-352) only clears pause + pending cancel, so an immediate `cancel(at_period_end=False)` (284-296) sets `status="canceled"` and is unrecoverable here. The verb set is exactly ensure_plan_provisioned/subscribe/set_seats/cancel/pause/resume/update_plan_prices — no upgrade/downgrade verb. Confirmed on every check.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** 03 has no competitor lifecycle-verb facts to cite, so this is best-practice grounded. Two distinct issues: (a) single-subscription-per-owner addressing is a reasonable simplification for UBB's one-plan model and only becomes a gap if multi-subscription is ever a goal — defer. (b) No plan upgrade/downgrade verb IS a real competitive gap: changing plan is table-stakes for SaaS billing, and `update_plan_prices`+`migrate_existing` only re-prices the *same* plan's axes, not a move to a different plan. The fix: add an `change_plan(customer, new_plan, proration_behavior)` verb that modifies the subscription items to the new plan's prices (mirror of `_migrate_axis_items`, service.py:439-471) and re-points `CustomerSubscriptionItem.plan`; ripple touches service.py, the item mirror, a new endpoint, and the SDK. Separately, immediate-cancel irreversibility should be documented as intentional (Stripe also can't un-cancel a hard-canceled sub). Recommend: build plan change; keep single-sub addressing.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** We can start, pause, resume and cancel a customer's subscription, but we can't move them from one plan to another — and that's a standard thing customers ask for. Worth building. Targeting "their one current subscription" is fine; hard-cancel being final is just how Stripe works too.

- Stripe-side changes that do NOT sync back: only `customer.subscription.created/updated/deleted` are handled (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/api/endpoints.py:145-149) — dashboard edits to Products/Prices never update `TenantBillingPlan` fees; `handle_subscription_updated` refreshes the `StripeSubscription` mirror aggregates but NOT the `CustomerSubscriptionItem` rows (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/api/webhooks.py:54-81); payment-method changes, Stripe-side coupons/trials, and pause/cancel have no local model beyond the pause_collection/cancel_at_period_end flags. POST `/subscriptions/sync` repairs subscription mirrors only — not plans, not items' axis history beyond what `_sum_items` derives.

  > **Verified — True.** Only `customer.subscription.created/updated/deleted` are registered (endpoints.py:145-149). `handle_subscription_updated` (webhooks.py:54-81) refreshes the `StripeSubscription` mirror's aggregates (amount_micros, quantity, interval, period, cancel_at_period_end, paused) but writes NOTHING to `CustomerSubscriptionItem` rows. No Product/Price webhook updates `TenantBillingPlan` fees. POST `/subscriptions/sync` repairs subscription mirrors only. Confirmed on all sub-claims.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** 03 doesn't catalogue competitor reverse-sync depth, so best practice governs: a mirror should converge to source-of-truth, and the asymmetry here (header aggregates refreshed, line items not) is a real consistency hazard — e.g. a dashboard seat-quantity edit updates `quantity` on the mirror but leaves `CustomerSubscriptionItem.quantity` stale, and the seat reconciler (next bullet) keys off items. The targeted fix: in `handle_subscription_updated`, reconcile the item rows from `stripe_sub["items"]["data"]` using the same axis-classification `_persist_mirror` already implements (service.py:541-572) — extract that into a shared helper both call. That closes the item drift with no new webhook and no migration. Plan-fee drift from dashboard Product/Price edits is a deliberate boundary (UBB owns plan fees; tenants shouldn't edit Prices in Stripe), so document it rather than subscribe to `price.updated`. Recommend: refactor the item-mirroring into one shared function so the webhook and orchestrator can't diverge — a real fix with a clean blast radius.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** When a subscription changes in Stripe's dashboard, we update the headline (amount, seat count) but not the itemized breakdown, which can quietly drift. Reusing the same line-mirroring code we already have on both the create and update paths fixes it cleanly. Letting people edit plan prices straight in Stripe stays off-limits on purpose.

- No periodic seat-quantity reconciler: a swallowed `seat.qty_push_failed` only self-corrects on the NEXT roster change (explicit note, ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/orchestration/seats.py:12-15). Seat counts: `seats >= 0` with no upper bound (ubb-platform/api/v1/schemas.py:431,435).

  > **Verified — True.** seats.py:12-15 states it outright: the push is full-state and "a missed push self-corrects on the next roster change; there is currently NO periodic seat-quantity reconciler." `_push` swallows `OrchestrationError` as `seat.qty_push_failed` (seats.py:96-99). `SeatsIn.seats = Field(ge=0)` and `SubscribeIn.seats = Field(default=0, ge=0)` (schemas.py:431,435) — lower bound 0, no upper bound. Confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** No competitor seat-reconciler facts in 03; best practice for any state mirrored to an external system is a periodic converger, and this codebase already has the exact pattern elsewhere (the Stage-D `reconcile_usage_drawdowns` hourly beat task and `reconcile_postpaid_usage`, tasks.py:96+). The fix is low-risk and idiomatic: add a beat task that, per business with an active seat item, recomputes `seat_count(business)` (seats.py:28-38) and calls `set_seats` when it differs from `CustomerSubscriptionItem.quantity` — a deterministic full-state push, so re-running is safe. Ripple: one new task + beat schedule entry, reusing existing orchestration; no schema or SDK change. This converts the current "self-heals only on the next roster change (which may never come for a stable roster)" into bounded convergence. The missing upper bound on seats is a minor input-hardening add (cap in `SeatsIn`/`SubscribeIn`) worth doing alongside. Recommend: add the reconciler — small, matches the house style, closes a silent-drift hole.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** If pushing a seat-count change to Stripe fails, it only retries the next time seats change — which might be never for a steady customer, so they could be billed for the wrong number of seats indefinitely. A small hourly job that recomputes and re-pushes seat counts (we already do exactly this for usage) fixes it.

- Postpaid close is strictly monthly, prior-calendar-month, UTC — no mid-month, threshold-triggered, or custom billing periods (ubb-platform/apps/billing/invoicing/tasks.py:64-93); push retry is bounded to 8 attempts/20h (inside Stripe's 24h idempotency window), then a permanent park requiring operator action (ubb-platform/config/settings.py:264-267).

  > **Verified — True.** `_prior_month()` (tasks.py:64-71) computes the prior calendar month; `close_postpaid_usage_periods` (74-93) iterates postpaid tenants over that fixed window — no mid-month, threshold, or custom-period path. Retry bound is `UBB_POSTPAID_PUSH_MAX_ATTEMPTS=8` / `UBB_POSTPAID_PUSH_MAX_AGE_HOURS=20` (settings.py:264-267), both inside Stripe's 24h idempotency window, then a terminal `failed_permanent` park requiring an operator (postpaid_service.py:126-136). Confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Competitors invoice on the subscription/billing-period clock with grace windows (03 Metronome: 24h post-period grace before finalize; 03 Orb: 12h pending window; 03 Lago: timestamp-based period assignment + premium draft grace period). UBB's strict prior-calendar-month is narrower: no threshold-triggered billing (bill when accrued usage crosses $X) and no period that follows a non-calendar subscription anchor — the latter directly conflicts with the anniversary-anchor feature in the earlier bullet, so the two should be designed together. The real competitive gap is threshold billing (common for high-volume AI usage) and anchor-aligned periods; the monthly-UTC default is a fine baseline. Fix is a scoped feature: parameterize the close window per tenant (and per subscription anchor), touching tasks.py, the `CustomerUsageInvoice` period keys, and the consolidation window. The 8-attempt/20h bound is correctly designed (stays inside the idempotency window) — leave it, but a tenant-facing alert on `failed_permanent` parking would help operability. Recommend: treat custom/threshold periods as a roadmap feature, not a quick fix.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Postpaid usage is always billed for the previous whole calendar month — there's no "bill them as soon as they hit $500" or aligning the usage bill to a customer's signup date. Those are real features customers want, best built together with anniversary billing. The retry limits are deliberately safe and fine as-is.
