- The line snapshot freezes at first claim: usage events that land in the period AFTER the claim are permanently excluded from that invoice (divergence is alert-only, `postpaid.snapshot_divergence` — ubb-platform/apps/billing/invoicing/services/postpaid_service.py:139-160); group_by changes mid-retry do not re-aggregate.

  > **Verified — True.** postpaid_service.py:142-160: when `rec.line_snapshot` already exists, the push consumes the frozen lines and recomputes the live aggregate only to log `postpaid.snapshot_divergence` on mismatch — "Alert-only, never mutate… the frozen lines are what bills." The freeze is set on first claim (161-164). The freeze comment (137-141) explains group_by changes mid-retry are deliberately NOT re-aggregated to avoid mis-indexed overbilling. Confirmed: late-arriving events are permanently excluded from that invoice (divergence is alert-only).
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Here competitors are clearly ahead and 03 is explicit: Metronome enforces a 24h post-period grace then finalizes, and can void+regenerate via `/invoices/regenerate` "using up-to-date usage" (03 Metronome); Orb keeps invoices pending 12h for late events and is "audit-safe… never overwrites or permanently deletes" (03 Orb); Lago's premium grace period keeps the invoice in draft N days so in-period late events still land before finalization (03 Lago). UBB's freeze-at-first-claim trades correctness for a no-double-bill guarantee on retries, and only ALERTS on divergence. The competitive fix is a grace window: delay the first claim until a configurable lag after period end (so most late events are already in), matching the industry 12-24h norm — a targeted change to when `push_customer_period` first claims, plus carrying late residual into the next period (the carry_in machinery already exists, postpaid_service.py:204). Re-aggregation mid-retry should stay forbidden (the indexing hazard is real). Recommend: add a grace delay before first claim; that closes most of the gap without reopening the overbill risk.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Once we start building a usage invoice, any usage that arrives late is left off it forever (we only log a warning). Competitors wait a day or so before finalizing so late events count. Adding a short grace delay before we lock the invoice would match them and is the right fix.

- `--rebill-void` is refused for consolidated rows (the target is the subscription renewal, not UBB's invoice — ubb-platform/apps/billing/invoicing/management/commands/repush_usage_invoice.py:48-64); a terminal row's pinned carry_in is parked, never auto-returned (postpaid_service.py:69-72).

  > **Verified — True.** repush_usage_invoice.py:48-64 raises a `CommandError` when `--rebill-void` is used on `invoice_kind == "consolidated"`, explaining the target is the customer's subscription renewal (Stripe-owned, auto-finalizing) and the rebill-void machinery would only re-resolve a NEW renewal draft, not void the old one. postpaid_service.py:69-72 confirms a terminal row keeps its pinned `carry_in_micros` PARKED, "never auto-returned… because the cent it funded may already sit on a finalized Stripe invoice." Confirmed both clauses.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is an internal operator-tooling guardrail, not a customer-facing capability, so competitor parity (03 has no facts here) isn't the right lens — it's a correctness decision and a good one: refusing an operation that can't actually void the Stripe-side renewal prevents a confident-but-wrong repush. The only honest improvement is operability: the parked carry_in is correct money-safety, but it's silent to the tenant — an operator must notice the `failed_permanent` row. Recommended (small) additions: emit/track a tenant-visible signal when carry_in is parked on a terminal row, and have the refusal message link the runbook step for handling the renewal in Stripe (it already describes the workaround). No service/webhook/migration/SDK ripple — this is doc + observability, not a code gap. Recommend: keep the refusal; add visibility for parked carry_in.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** When a usage charge has been folded into a Stripe-managed subscription renewal, our internal "void and rebill" tool correctly refuses, because it can't actually undo the Stripe invoice — that's the safe choice. The only thing to improve is making the leftover parked balance visible so an operator doesn't miss it.

- The usage-invoice consolidation window is ~45 minutes after the cycle anchor (`CONSOLIDATION_MAX_DRAFT_AGE_SECONDS`, postpaid_service.py:17); a paused or non-UBB-managed subscription is never consolidated (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/ports.py:23-49).

  > **Verified — True.** `CONSOLIDATION_MAX_DRAFT_AGE_SECONDS = 45 * 60` (postpaid_service.py:17); `_find_renewal_draft` falls back to standalone when the draft is older than that, unageable, or won't auto-advance (482-490), because Stripe auto-finalizes the renewal draft ~1h after the anchor and pinning into a finalizing draft forks the split path. `get_active_subscription_for_consolidation` (ports.py:23-49) returns None for a paused sub (`paused=False` filter) or one with no UBB-plan item (`line_items__plan__isnull=False`), so a paused or non-UBB-managed subscription is never consolidated. Confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** No 03 facts on competitor consolidation windows; this is best-practice and internal-mechanics territory. The 45-minute window is a defensible safety margin against Stripe's ~1h auto-finalize, and the standalone fallback means usage is never lost — it just bills on its own invoice instead of riding the renewal. So this is correctness, not a gap: the design fails safe. The honest improvements are observability and tuning: the window is a hard-coded constant (not tenant-configurable), and the `postpaid.consolidation_window_missed` / `consolidation_no_active_subscription` logs are operator-only — a tenant has no signal that consolidation didn't happen. Recommended small steps: surface a consolidation-missed metric/event, and consider making the window a setting (settings.py) so it can be tuned if Stripe's finalize timing shifts. Not consolidating a paused subscription is deliberately correct (a paused draft may never finalize, so pinned items would never bill). Recommend: keep behavior; add tunability + a tenant-facing signal.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** We only fold usage into a Stripe subscription renewal if we catch the draft within ~45 minutes of it opening; miss that and the usage simply bills on its own invoice — so nothing is lost, it's a safe fallback. The window is reasonable; we should just make it adjustable and visible when it's missed.

- The AR payment_status transition table is strict: paid and void are final — a Stripe-reported regression (e.g. paid→open) is logged and never applied (ubb-platform/apps/billing/connectors/stripe/invoice_routing.py:59-69; ubb-platform/apps/billing/invoicing/tasks.py:226-238). GET `/subscriptions/customers/{id}/invoices` lists PAID invoices only (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/api/endpoints.py:89-93); open/uncollectible subscription invoices are visible to tenants only via the AR fields, and to end customers via `/me/subscription-invoices`.

  > **Verified — True.** `AR_ALLOWED` (invoice_routing.py:59-65) makes `paid` and `void` terminal (empty allowed-sets); `ar_transition_allowed` (68-69) governs both the usage-invoice reconcile (tasks.py:226-238) and the subscription-invoice repair (ports.py:87-118), and an illegal transition like paid→open is logged `ar.reconcile_unexpected_regression` and never applied. `get_invoices` filters `paid_at__isnull=False` (endpoints.py:89-93) — PAID only. End-customers see subscription invoices via `/me/subscription-invoices` (me_endpoints.py:416), which lists ALL statuses for the billing owner. Confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** 03 has no competitor AR-transition facts; best practice agrees with the design — Stripe itself treats paid/void as terminal, so refusing a reported regression (rather than corrupting local state) is correct, and routing both paths through one shared table is exactly right for consistency. This is not a gap. The only real usability issue is the tenant-facing read: `get_invoices` exposes PAID invoices only, so a tenant using the subscriptions read API can't list open/uncollectible subscription invoices except by reading individual AR fields. Recommended small improvement: add a `status` filter (or an `include_unpaid`/all-status listing) to `GET /subscriptions/customers/{id}/invoices` so tenants can see outstanding invoices, not just collected revenue — a contained endpoint + schema change, no migration, plus an SDK passthrough. Keep the strict transition table. Recommend: relax only the read-side filter, not the state machine.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Once an invoice is paid or voided we never let a late Stripe report flip it back — that's the correct, safe behavior. The one rough edge is that our subscription-invoice listing shows only paid invoices, so a customer-platform can't easily pull a list of who still owes money; adding an unpaid/all filter to that endpoint is a small, worthwhile add.

- `invoice.payment_failed` unconditionally SUSPENDS the matched customer (ubb-platform/apps/billing/connectors/stripe/webhooks.py:218-231) — a tenant cannot opt a customer out of suspension-on-failed-invoice on this surface; reactivation is not exposed here.

  > **Verified — True.** stripe/webhooks.py:208-231: after stamping `payment_failed_at`, the handler looks up the matched customer and, unless already suspended, sets `customer.status = "suspended"` unconditionally — no tenant flag is consulted, and a suspended seat triggers a seat-count re-push. There is no reactivation verb on the platform surface (the lifecycle verbs are cancel/pause/resume on the subscription, not customer reactivation). Confirmed: a tenant cannot opt a customer out of suspend-on-failed-invoice here, and un-suspend isn't exposed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** 03 records no competitor dunning/suspension-policy facts, so best practice governs: dunning is normally configurable (retry schedule, grace before suspend, soft vs hard), and Stripe Billing itself exposes Smart Retries + configurable subscription behavior on failure. Unconditional immediate suspend on the FIRST `invoice.payment_failed` is aggressive and almost certainly should be tenant-configurable, not removed: the suspend itself is a reasonable default for a usage platform that must stop accruing cost, but "suspend on first failure, with no opt-out and no exposed reactivation" is a footgun for tenants who want a grace period or rely on Stripe's retries. Recommended fix: add a tenant config flag (e.g. `suspend_on_payment_failure`, defaulting to current behavior) read in the handler, and expose a reactivation endpoint that flips `status` back to active and re-pushes the seat count. Ripple: a `TenantConfig` field + migration, a few lines in webhooks.py, a new platform endpoint, and an SDK method. Recommend: make it configurable and add reactivation — a real operability gap.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** The instant a customer's payment fails, we suspend them, every time, with no way to opt out and no exposed button to turn them back on. The suspend is a sensible default to stop runaway costs, but it should be a setting tenants can soften, and there must be a way to reactivate — both are worth building.

- No plan list/GET/DELETE endpoints (platform_endpoints.py has only POST `/plans` and PATCH `/plans/{key}`); PATCH cannot change interval/name/usage_mode.

  > **Verified — True.** platform_api exposes only POST `/plans` (platform_endpoints.py:122-138) and PATCH `/plans/{key}` (141-172) — no list, GET-by-key, or DELETE route. PATCH takes `PlanUpdateIn` = `access_fee_micros`/`per_seat_micros`/`migrate_existing` only (schemas.py:418-422), so it cannot change `interval`, `name`, or `usage_mode`. Confirmed: no read/delete surface, and PATCH is fee-only.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is CRUD completeness, not a competitive differentiator (03 has no relevant facts) — and it's the cheapest win after interval validation. A tenant today can create and re-price a plan but cannot list their plans, fetch one, or remove an obsolete one via API; they'd have to track keys out-of-band. Fix is trivial and low-risk: add GET `/plans` (list) and GET `/plans/{key}` returning the existing `PlanOut`, and a DELETE `/plans/{key}` guarded against deleting a plan with active subscriptions (refuse with 409 if any `CustomerSubscriptionItem` references it, since provisioned Stripe Prices/Products live on the connected account). Extending PATCH to set `name` is safe (cosmetic); `interval` should only be PATCHable before provisioning (after provisioning it's baked into the Stripe Price). Ripple: a handful of endpoint functions reusing `_plan_out`, plus SDK list/get/delete wrappers; no migration. Recommend: add list/GET now (trivial), add guarded DELETE and name-PATCH; gate interval-PATCH on unprovisioned only.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** A customer-platform can create and re-price plans through the API but can't list them, look one up, or delete an old one — basic gaps that are quick to fill. Adding read and a safe delete is low-effort housekeeping that makes the plan API feel finished.

- `plan.usage_mode` ('invoice_item'|'none') is dead config at HEAD: written and echoed but read by no billing code path (auditor grep: refs limited to ubb-platform/api/v1/platform_endpoints.py:118,134 + schemas + migration); whether usage is invoiced is governed solely by `tenant.billing_mode='postpaid'`.

  > **Verified — True.** Grepping `usage_mode` across ubb-platform returns only schemas.py (PlanIn/PlanOut), platform_endpoints.py:118,134 (echoed into `_plan_out` and written on create), models.py:91 (the column), the seed command, one migration, and a model test — NO billing/invoicing/postpaid code path reads it. Whether usage is invoiced is governed solely by `tenant.billing_mode == "postpaid"` (tasks.py:83, the close iterates `billing_mode="postpaid"` tenants). Confirmed: written and echoed, read by no billing logic.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** No competitor facts apply; this is internal hygiene. Dead config is a liability — it implies a per-plan capability (turn usage invoicing on/off per plan) that doesn't exist, so a tenant could set `usage_mode="none"` and still be billed for usage because the real switch is tenant-level `billing_mode`. Two honest options: (1) remove it — drop the field from `PlanIn`/`PlanOut`/`_plan_out`/model via a migration (cleanest, but a breaking API/schema change and a column drop), or (2) wire it up — make the postpaid close skip customers whose subscription plan has `usage_mode="none"`, turning it into a real per-plan usage-billing toggle (a genuine feature: mix metered-and-not plans under one postpaid tenant). Given the codebase already resolves plan per subscription, option 2 is plausible but is a real billing-logic change (touch `close_postpaid_usage_periods`/`push_customer_period`, careful with seats/business aggregation). Recommend: decide deliberately — if there's no near-term need for per-plan usage toggling, remove the field to stop it lying; otherwise wire it into the postpaid close. Do not leave it dead.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Plans carry a "usage mode" setting that does absolutely nothing — usage billing is actually decided at the customer-platform level. That's misleading and should either be deleted or actually hooked up to mean what it implies; leaving it as decoration invites mistakes.


### 5.4 Hierarchy & end-customer widget

- The account hierarchy is exactly one level: seats under a business; a seat cannot be a parent; business/seat types and topology are fixed at create (no PATCH endpoint to convert account_type or re-parent) (ubb-platform/api/v1/platform_endpoints.py:37-81).

  > **Verified — True.** Confirmed at platform_endpoints.py:37-81. `create_customer` accepts `account_type` in {individual, business, seat}; a seat MUST name a `parent_external_id` whose `account_type="business"` (line 48-52) — so a seat can never be a parent, capping depth at one level. `account_type`, `parent`, and `billing_topology` are written only inside `Customer.objects.create(...)` (lines 60-67) and there is NO PATCH/convert/re-parent route: a grep of platform_endpoints.py finds PATCH only on `/plans/{key}` and POST verbs for subscribe/seats/cancel/pause/resume — none mutate account_type or parent. The doc's anchor is accurate.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** No competitor fact in 03 speaks to N-level account trees, so per the evidence rule this is best-practice framing, not a competitor gap: a single business→seat tier covers the common "company buys, team consumes" case, and deeper org trees (region→dept→team) are rare in usage billing. This reads as a deliberate scope choice, not a bug. If multi-level is wanted later, the ripple is contained: `Customer.resolve_billing_owner()` would need to walk parents recursively instead of one hop, the create endpoint would drop the `account_type="business"` parent filter, and an `account_type`/`parent` PATCH (with a cycle guard and a wallet-migration story) would be added — none of which is forced now.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** You can model "a company and its individual users," but not deeper org charts, and once you create an account you cannot later change its type or move it under a different parent. For most customers that is fine; it is a scoping decision, not a defect.

- `/me` API: a pooled seat sees EMPTY usage-invoice and subscription-invoice lists (owner gate, ubb-platform/api/v1/me_endpoints.py:334-338,422-425) and an empty own-wallet grants list; `/me/grants` is hard-capped at 100 lots with no pagination (166-191); usage-summary is fixed to current-UTC-month-to-date — no historical periods (382-413). No widget endpoints for cancel/pause, payment methods, or plan info. Widget JWTs are HS256 with a single per-tenant secret; no aud/scope claims (ubb-platform/core/widget_auth.py:10-18).

  > **Verified — True, with one nuance.** All cited gates confirmed in me_endpoints.py: usage-invoices returns empty for a non-owner seat (`resolve_billing_owner().id != customer.id`, lines 337-338), subscription-invoices applies the same gate (424-425), and `/me/grants` is hard-capped at `[:100]` with no cursor (185-186). usage-summary is fixed to current-UTC-month-to-date (period_start = first of month, period_end = today+1; lines 401-403) with no period params. widget JWTs are HS256 with the per-tenant `widget_secret` and carry only sub/tid/iss/exp — no aud/scope (widget_auth.py:10-18, verified). **Nuance:** the empty lists are deliberate per-seat privacy (the code comments at 334-338 say surfacing the consolidated business bill "would leak sibling spend"), NOT a bug — usage-summary intentionally has NO owner gate so a seat still sees its own consumption (389-396).
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Evidence: Metronome ships "Embeddable Dashboards" as a first-class status-page component (03 Metronome, status page). UBB's widget is read-only and thinner. Best-practice fixes, all deliberate-design-aware: (a) keep the privacy gate but add an opt-in business-token view so a pooled seat's admin can see the consolidated bill; (b) add `start_date`/`end_date` to usage-summary for historical periods (the underlying `get_customer_usage_summary` already takes a range); (c) paginate `/me/grants` with the same cursor helper the tenant grants list uses; (d) add `aud`/`scope` claims to widget JWTs (widget_auth + SDK token mint) for least-privilege tokens. None of these touch money paths.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** The end-customer widget is intentionally privacy-walled (a team member can't see the shared company bill) and minimal: this-month-only usage, no self-service cancel/pause. That privacy is correct; the gaps to consider are historical views and a richer embeddable portal like Metronome's.

- No HTTP endpoint mints widget tokens — tenants must run the SDK (or equivalent `jwt.encode`) server-side with `widget_secret` + `tenant_id` (ubb-sdk/ubb/client.py:91-107).

  > **Verified — True.** A repo-wide grep for `create_widget_token`/widget-token shows it defined only in core/widget_auth.py (and seed/tests) — NOT in any NinjaAPI endpoint module. The SDK mints the JWT locally with `jwt.encode(payload, widget_secret, algorithm="HS256")` (client.py:91-107), requiring the tenant to hold `widget_secret` + `tenant_id` server-side. So tenants on non-Python stacks must reimplement the exact HS256 encode themselves. Confirmed.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** No 03 fact covers a competitor token-mint endpoint, so this is best-practice framing. The design (sign locally, never round-trip the secret) is defensible — it avoids an HTTP call per widget load and keeps the secret off the wire. The cost is polyglot friction: a Node/Go/Ruby tenant cannot use the Python helper. Two non-exclusive fixes: (a) add an authenticated `POST /api/v1/widget/token` that mints the JWT server-side from the API key (one new endpoint, reuses `create_widget_token`, no model change) so any language can call it; and/or (b) publish SDKs in more languages — Orb ships 6 (Python, TypeScript, Go, Java, Kotlin, Ruby) and Metronome 4 (Python, Node, Ruby, Go) per 03, while UBB has one. Either removes the reimplement-HS256 burden.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Today only the Python SDK can hand an end-customer a login token for the widget; teams on other languages must hand-roll the crypto. Adding a tiny "give me a token" API call, or more language SDKs, fixes that — competitors like Orb and Metronome ship several SDKs.


### 5.5 Platform, config & operability

- No self-serve tenant signup: no API endpoint creates a live Tenant — bootstrap is seed_dev_data/Django admin only (auditor grep: no `Tenant.objects.create` outside tests/seed; ubb-platform/config/urls.py has no signup route).

  > **Verified —** True. Grep for `Tenant.objects.create`/`Tenant.all_objects.create` under `ubb-platform/api/` matches ONLY test files (28 files, all `tests/`); `config/urls.py` (lines 21-41) mounts no signup/registration route — every path is `api/v1/...` behind `ApiKeyAuth`. A live Tenant is born only via `seed_dev_data` or Django admin (`admin/` at urls.py:22). Confirmed by the absence check, not just the doc.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Orb keys are "created self-serve in the webapp (Organization Settings)" (03 Orb, withorb.com/api-reference) and Metronome tokens are "created in the app" (03 Metronome, docs.metronome.com/api-reference/authentication) — but both presuppose an already-provisioned org; neither documents an unauthenticated *org-creation* API either (signup is a web flow). So this is NOT a competitive gap: pre-PMF B2B billing infra is universally sales-/console-onboarded, not open public signup (fraud and Stripe-Connect KYC make open signup actively undesirable). Recommendation: keep as a deliberate choice. If self-serve is ever wanted, the clean shape is a separate unauthenticated `signup_api` (its own NinjaAPI, not `ApiKeyAuth`) that creates the Tenant + first key in one transaction and emits a `tenant.created` event — isolated from `tenant_api`, no ripple into existing auth.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** You cannot sign up for UBB through the API today; a human provisions each customer. That is normal and even safer for billing software at this stage — not something rivals do differently in a way that matters.

- Tenant config PATCH cannot change: name, min_balance_micros, hard_stop_balance_micros, run_cost_limit_micros, platform_fee_percentage, backfill_window_days, branding_config, metadata — none are in `TenantConfigIn` (ubb-platform/api/v1/schemas.py:389-396 vs ubb-platform/apps/platform/tenants/models.py:30-64).

  > **Verified —** True. `TenantConfigIn` (schemas.py:389-396) exposes exactly five mutable fields: `billing_mode`, `products`, `require_cost_card_coverage`, `automatic_tax_enabled`, `default_currency`. The `Tenant` model (models.py:30-64) additionally holds `name`, `min_balance_micros`, `run_cost_limit_micros`, `hard_stop_balance_micros`, `platform_fee_percentage`, `backfill_window_days`, `branding_config`, `metadata` — none in the input schema, so PATCH cannot touch them. Confirmed by field-by-field diff.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This mixes two categories. `platform_fee_percentage` SHOULD stay tenant-immutable — a tenant editing its own platform fee is a revenue-integrity hole (UBB's own pricing terms; best practice: operator-only). But `name`, `min_balance_micros`, `hard_stop_balance_micros`, `run_cost_limit_micros`, `backfill_window_days`, `branding_config`, `metadata` are ordinary self-service config; making them un-PATCHable forces console/ORM round-trips. The fix is low-ripple: add the safe subset to `TenantConfigIn` (all `Optional`) and have the existing `PATCH /config` handler apply them under the same `model.clean()` guards (clean already bounds `backfill_window_days` 0-60, models.py:110-113), leaving fee + currency-lock logic untouched. Keep `platform_fee_percentage` out of the schema by design.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Customers can self-edit only a handful of settings; basics like their display name, low-balance thresholds and branding still require us to do it for them. We should open up the harmless ones and keep our own fee rate locked.

- 'metering' can never be removed from products; prepaid/postpaid billing_mode without the 'billing' product is rejected (ubb-platform/apps/platform/tenants/models.py:99-109).

  > **Verified —** True. `Tenant.clean()` (models.py:96-109) raises if `"metering" not in products` and raises if `billing_mode` is `prepaid`/`postpaid` without `"billing"` in products. `save()` (models.py:115-124) also force-defaults products to `["metering"]` and re-runs `clean()`, so the invariant holds on every write including PATCH.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is a correct architectural invariant, not a gap: metering is the substrate every other capability (pricing, drawdown, margin, invoicing) reads from, and prepaid/postpaid genuinely require the billing machinery. Competitors bundle equivalently — OpenMeter is literally "the metering and billing platform" with metering as the base layer (03 OpenMeter), and Lago/Orb/Metronome have no notion of billing without metered events. No evidence anyone lets you run usage billing with metering disabled. Recommendation: keep exactly as is; the only improvement worth considering is a clearer 422 message distinguishing "metering is mandatory" from "this billing_mode needs the billing product" (the two `ValidationError`s already do this — adequate). No patch needed.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Metering is always on because everything else is built on top of it, and you cannot pick paid billing modes without the billing add-on. This is the right design and matches how every competitor is structured.

- API keys: cannot revoke the last active key (409); no key scopes/permissions, no expiry, no IP allowlists; the raw key is irretrievable after the mint/rotate response; `last_used_at` lags up to 5 min (ubb-platform/api/v1/tenant_endpoints.py:250-282; ubb-platform/config/settings.py:208-211).

  > **Verified —** True on every clause. `revoke_api_key` (tenant_endpoints.py:250-282) returns 409 `last_active_key` when revoking the last active key, under `select_for_update` so concurrent revokes can't race past it. `TenantApiKey` (models.py:133-139) has `key_prefix`/`key_hash`/`label`/`is_active` — NO scope, expiry, or IP-allowlist fields. Raw key returned once at mint (line 210 "shown ONCE") and rotate (line 246); never re-derivable from `key_hash`. `last_used_at` is Redis-buffered, flushed by `flush-api-key-last-used` on `crontab(minute="*/5")` (settings.py:208-211) — up to 5 min lag, as the docstring at tenant_endpoints.py:175-177 states.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Scopes are a real, evidenced gap: Metronome tokens "CAN be scoped by Access level (read-only), Environment, and Endpoint" (03 Metronome, docs.metronome.com/api-reference/authentication) — though scope changes are not self-serve. Orb, by contrast, documents NO fine-grained key scopes (03 Orb). Irretrievable-raw-key matches best practice and Metronome ("You cannot view the full token again"). No competitor evidence demands key expiry or IP allowlists. The last-active-key 409 and 5-min `last_used_at` lag are deliberate, sensible (lockout guard; write-batching). Fix worth doing: add an optional `scopes` JSON column to `TenantApiKey` + a migration, enforced in `core.auth.ApiKeyAuth`, defaulting to full access (read-only being the high-value scope). Expiry/IP-allowlist are nice-to-haves, defer.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** API keys work but are coarse: every key is all-powerful, with no read-only or scoped keys like Metronome offers. Adding a read-only scope is the one upgrade that matters; the other limits (can't delete your last key, slightly stale "last used" time) are intentional and fine.

- Sandbox: exactly one per tenant (`uq_one_sandbox_per_parent`), no nested sandboxes, no sandbox delete endpoint; reset is async (202) with the sandbox 401ing mid-wipe and left inactive on partial failure; no config-promotion/copy-to-live endpoint (ubb-platform/apps/platform/tenants/models.py:78-83; ubb-platform/apps/platform/tenants/tasks.py:126-131).

  > **Verified —** True. `uq_one_sandbox_per_parent` + `ck_sandbox_iff_parent` (models.py:78-91) enforce one sandbox per parent and no nesting. Endpoints (tenant_endpoints.py:288-323) offer only POST `/sandbox` (create/re-mint key) and GET `/sandbox` (status) — no DELETE, no promote/copy-to-live. Reset (tasks.py:126-144) leaves the sandbox `is_active` unchanged on partial failure and raises `RuntimeError`, then flips `is_active=True` only on full success; mid-wipe the sandbox 401s. The async-202 reset entrypoint is `reset_sandbox_tenant` (tasks.py:147+).
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Orb has a distinct Test Mode with self-serve test-mode keys (03 Orb, docs.withorb.com/quickstart/ingest); Metronome runs a Sandbox environment alongside production (03 Metronome). Lago has NO sandbox at all and tells users to run separate accounts (03 Lago, getlago.com/.../integration-testing) — so UBB's one-sandbox-per-tenant already beats Lago. No competitor documents nested sandboxes or a config-promotion endpoint, so those aren't gaps. The real ergonomics gap is no config-promotion/copy-to-live: teams want to build pricing/webhooks in sandbox then ship to live. Fix: add a `POST /sandbox/promote` in `sandbox_service` that copies the whitelisted config models (rate cards, webhook configs, plans) sandbox→parent in one transaction. A sandbox DELETE is low value (reset covers it). Leave the inactive-on-failure behavior — it is the correct fail-safe.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Each customer gets one sandbox to test in, which already beats Lago (none) and matches Orb/Metronome. The missing piece is a one-click "promote my tested config to live" — worth building. A broken reset correctly leaves the sandbox switched off rather than half-wiped.

- Sandbox Stripe: requires `STRIPE_TEST_SECRET_KEY` (sk_test_) configured server-side or every sandbox Stripe call fails loudly; a sandbox can never be platform-fee invoiced (ubb-platform/apps/billing/stripe/services/stripe_service.py:47-54,157-160).

  > **Verified —** True. `api_key_for_tenant` (stripe_service.py:40-55) returns `STRIPE_TEST_SECRET_KEY` for a sandbox tenant and raises `StripeFatalError` if it is missing or not `sk_test_` — so every sandbox Stripe call fails loudly without it. `create_platform_fee_invoice` (stripe_service.py:157-160) hard-raises for any `is_sandbox` tenant, so a sandbox can never be platform-fee invoiced.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This mirrors how rivals wire test environments to test Stripe: Metronome "automatically connects to your Stripe test mode" when Stripe is connected in Sandbox (03 Metronome, docs.metronome.com/integrations/.../stripe), and Orb deliberately isolates test mode "so test mode workloads do not affect live mode" (03 Orb). The refuse-live guard (must be `sk_test_`) is exactly the right safety stance — it prevents sandbox traffic leaking onto the live Stripe account. The only fix is operability, not design: surface the missing-key state as a clear sandbox-provisioning precheck (e.g. `GET /sandbox` could report `stripe_test_configured: false`) so an operator sees it before the first sandbox Stripe call dies, rather than discovering it via a `StripeFatalError`. No model/migration ripple.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Sandboxes need a Stripe test key configured on our side, and we refuse to ever bill a sandbox for real — both correct and matching Metronome/Orb. The only nicety is warning operators up front when the test key is missing instead of failing on first use.

- Webhook configs: no PATCH/update (delete + recreate to change url/secret/filters), no test-delivery/ping endpoint, no tenant-facing delivery-attempt/log API, no secret-rotation primitive (single secret per config; the SDK verifier accepts multiple `v1=` sigs but the sender only ever signs with one secret) (ubb-platform/apps/platform/events/api/webhook_endpoints.py:27-79; ubb-platform/apps/platform/events/webhooks.py:147-150).

  > **Verified —** True. `webhook_endpoints.py` exposes only POST `/configs`, GET `/configs`, DELETE `/configs/{id}` (lines 27-79) — no PATCH, no test-ping, no delivery-log route. To change url/secret/event_types you must delete and recreate. The sender signs with the single `config.secret` per config (webhooks.py:147-150) — `compute_signature` + `compute_signature_v2` both take one secret — even though the SDK verifier accepts multiple `v1=` sigs, so there is no rotation primitive.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Real ergonomics gaps, and Stripe is the bar: Stripe lets you "change the events that a webhook endpoint receives ... with the API," and "roll (change)" the signing secret with a grace window where "multiple secrets remain active and Stripe generates one signature per secret," plus test/resend events (Stripe webhooks docs, fetched 2026-06-16). Orb publishes a Webhooks component with 99.96% uptime (03 Orb status page) implying first-class webhook management. The fix is mostly additive, low-ripple: add `PATCH /configs/{id}` (re-validate url via `validate_webhook_url`); add `POST /configs/{id}/test` that delivers a synthetic `webhook.test` event through `_deliver_to_config`; for rotation, change `TenantWebhookConfig.secret` to a small set of active secrets (or add `secret_next` + `rotated_at`) and have `_deliver_to_config` sign with each — the SDK verifier ALREADY accepts multiple `v1=`, so the receiver side needs no change. This touches `webhook_models` (+migration) and `webhooks.py` only.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Customers can only create or delete webhooks, not edit them, send a test ping, or rotate the secret without downtime — all things Stripe does. These are genuine usability gaps worth closing, and the secret-rotation half is half-built already (our verifier accepts multiple signatures).

- Webhook secrets are caller-supplied (min 32 chars) and stored in PLAINTEXT in `ubb_tenant_webhook_config.secret` (ubb-platform/apps/platform/events/webhook_models.py:13).

  > **Verified —** True — and a genuine security gap. `WebhookConfigCreateRequest.secret` is `Field(min_length=32, max_length=255)` (webhook_endpoints.py:11), stored straight onto `TenantWebhookConfig.secret = models.CharField(max_length=255, ...)` (webhook_models.py:13) with no hashing/encryption. The sender reads it back in cleartext to HMAC each delivery (webhooks.py:147,150), so a DB read or backup leak exposes every tenant's signing secret.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Encryption at rest is table stakes for the field: Metronome "encrypts your data ... at rest ... AES256-GCM" (03 Metronome, metronome.com/company/security) and Orb encrypts "all production data ... at rest" (03 Orb, withorb.com/security). A webhook secret is symmetric — the sender must recover the plaintext to sign — so a one-way hash is NOT an option here (unlike a password). The correct fix is application-level encryption-at-rest: store `secret` encrypted under a `WEBHOOK_SECRET_KEY` (Fernet/`cryptography`), decrypt only in `_deliver_to_config`. Ripple: an `encrypted_secret` column + a data migration to re-encrypt existing rows, an encrypt-on-write/decrypt-on-read accessor on `webhook_models`, and key management in settings. This also pairs naturally with the rotation work in the prior bullet. Server-generated secrets (returned once) would additionally remove weak caller secrets.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Webhook signing secrets are stored in plain text in our database — a real security weakness, since anyone who reads the DB can forge webhooks. Both Metronome and Orb encrypt this kind of data at rest; we should encrypt it too (we can't just hash it, because we need it back to sign).

- Webhook URLs: https only, public IPs only — no http, no localhost/private ranges even for development (ubb-platform/core/url_validation.py:24-46).

  > **Verified —** True. `validate_webhook_url` (url_validation.py:6-53) rejects any non-`https` scheme (line 24), rejects literal localhost/loopback (line 32), and resolves the hostname and rejects any `is_private`/`is_loopback`/`is_link_local`/`is_reserved` IP (lines 43-46) including the AWS metadata address — with no environment/dev bypass anywhere in the function.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is a deliberate, correct SSRF defense, not a gap — it is exactly the hardening (DNS-rebind pin to the validated IP, metadata-endpoint block) that mature webhook senders implement, and no competitor advertises delivering to private/HTTP endpoints. The only friction is local development: a dev cannot point a webhook at `http://localhost:4000`. Recommendation: keep the production stance unchanged but add a narrow, settings-gated dev override — e.g. honor an `ALLOW_INSECURE_WEBHOOK_URLS` flag (default False, never True in prod settings) that relaxes the scheme/private-IP checks, OR document the standard tunnel workaround (ngrok/cloudflared gives an https public URL). Touches `url_validation.py` + `settings.py` only; do not weaken the default.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Webhooks must go to real public HTTPS addresses, which blocks a class of server-side attacks — the right call for production. The only cost is that local testing needs a tunnel; we could add a clearly-flagged dev-only escape hatch.

- Webhook delivery: at-least-once with NO per-config checkpoint — the `HandlerCheckpoint` is per event+handler, so if one config's POST fails, the retry re-POSTs to ALL matching configs including ones that already succeeded; receivers must dedupe on `event_id` (ubb-platform/apps/platform/events/dispatch.py:59-77; ubb-platform/apps/platform/events/webhooks.py:105-132).

  > **Verified —** True. `HandlerCheckpoint` is keyed on (outbox_event, handler_name) (dispatch.py:60-77), and `deliver_webhook` is registered ONCE as a single handler `platform.webhook_delivery.{event_type}` (apps.py:16-22) that loops over ALL active matching configs (webhooks.py:111-132). So the checkpoint records "the delivery handler ran for this event," not "this config got it" — a retry that fails on one config re-POSTs to every matching config. Receivers must dedupe on `event_id` (payload carries `event_id`, webhooks.py:141).
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** At-least-once + receiver-side idempotency is the industry norm, so the contract is fine: Stripe webhooks and Orb both deliver at-least-once and expect dedupe (Orb runs a dedicated Webhooks component, 03 Orb status). The genuine defect is the fan-out re-POST: a flaky receiver on config B causes config A to be hammered with duplicates on every retry. Fix: make the checkpoint per (event, config) — i.e. register/track delivery at config granularity, or write a `WebhookDeliveryAttempt` success row (the model ALREADY exists, webhook_models.py:28-46) and skip configs that already have a success for this event before re-POSTing. This is contained to `dispatch.py`/`webhooks.py` + using the existing attempt table; no schema change needed. Keep the at-least-once guarantee.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** If you have two webhook URLs and one is flaky, our retries re-send to the healthy one too, so it sees duplicates. At-least-once delivery is normal and fine, but we should track success per-URL so a retry only re-sends to the URL that actually failed.

- Webhook retries are bounded: 5 retries over ~2h43m (30s/2m/10m/30m/2h) then dead-letter status='failed' with a CRITICAL log; no tenant-facing redelivery API — recovery is operator/ORM-level (ubb-platform/apps/platform/events/models.py:24; ubb-platform/apps/platform/events/tasks.py:20-26,70-72).

  > **Verified —** True. `OutboxEvent.max_retries` defaults to 5 (models.py:24); `BACKOFF_SCHEDULE = [30, 120, 600, 1800, 7200]` (tasks.py:20) = 30s/2m/10m/30m/2h ≈ 2h43m total; on exhaustion `status="failed"` and `alert_dead_letter` logs CRITICAL (tasks.py:70-72, 29-43). No tenant-facing redelivery route exists in `webhook_endpoints.py` — recovery is operator/ORM only.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Bounded retry + dead-letter is standard, but a tenant-facing redelivery API is the expected recovery affordance and a real gap: Stripe lets you manually **Resend** an event "for up to 15 days" via dashboard and `stripe events resend` via CLI (Stripe webhooks docs, fetched 2026-06-16). Orb surfaces webhook health on a status page (03 Orb) implying tenant visibility. The fix layers on the prior two: expose `GET /configs/{id}/deliveries` (read the existing `WebhookDeliveryAttempt` rows, webhook_models.py:28) and `POST /deliveries/{id}/redeliver` (or `POST /configs/{id}/replay?event_id=`) that re-enqueues `_deliver_to_config` for that one config/event. Self-contained to `webhook_endpoints.py` + a thin task; no model change (attempt table already logs status_code/success/error). Keep the ~2h43m bound and CRITICAL dead-letter alert.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** We retry a failing webhook for about 2h43m then give up and alert ourselves, but a customer cannot see the failed deliveries or replay them — they have to ask us. Stripe lets customers resend events themselves; we should expose the same, and we already log every attempt so the data is there.

- The event catalog is fixed at the 26 registered types; `customer.deleted` is internal-only (not deliverable); no custom/tenant-defined event types (ubb-platform/apps/platform/events/catalog.py; ubb-platform/apps/platform/events/schemas.py:89-93).

  > **Verified —** True (as of the 2026-06-12 audit). `apps.py` registered exactly 25 event types (counted); the catalog is now **26** — `run.limit_exceeded` was added 2026-06-19, and on 2026-06-23 the list was extracted to a single source of truth at `events/catalog.py` (iterated by `apps.py` `ready()`). `customer.deleted` exists as a `CustomerDeleted` schema (schemas.py:89-93) but is NOT in the registered list, so it is internal-only and never delivered. There is no mechanism for tenant-defined event types — the registry is a static list bound at app `ready()`.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** A fixed first-party catalog is normal for billing platforms (Stripe, Orb, Metronome all emit a fixed set of system events; none of the 03 evidence shows tenant-authored custom webhook event *types*). So "no custom event types" is not a competitive gap — billing events are inherently system-defined. The honest framing: 26 covers usage/billing/referral/margin/budget/run/sandbox/api-key lifecycle, which is broad. Recommendation: no custom-event mechanism needed; if `customer.deleted` should be observable by tenants, the trivial fix is to register it (add to `events/catalog.py`) — verify first that no internal-only assumption depends on its non-delivery. Otherwise no patch.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** We emit a fixed menu of 26 event types and customers can't invent their own — which is exactly how billing platforms work, so it's not a gap. One small call: decide whether "customer deleted" should be a customer-visible event (today it's internal-only).

- List endpoints (billing-periods, invoices) cap limit at 100 per page (ubb-platform/api/v1/tenant_endpoints.py:50,90).

  > **Verified —** True. Both `list_billing_periods` (tenant_endpoints.py:48,50) and `list_invoices` (lines 88,90) do `limit = min(max(limit, 1), 100)`, hard-capping the page size at 100. Both are cursor-paginated (`encode_cursor`/`apply_cursor_filter`, has_more/next_cursor), so the cap bounds page size, not total reachable rows.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** A 100-item page cap with cursor pagination is squarely industry-standard — it matches Metronome's documented ingest batch cap "maxItems: 100" and the general 100-per-page convention across these APIs (03 Metronome). Orb's SDKs "include built-in support for ... pagination" (03 Orb) for exactly this. Because pagination is cursor-based and forward-complete, nothing is unreachable. Recommendation: keep as is — this is correct API hygiene, not a gap. The only thing to ensure is that the SDK transparently auto-paginates these list endpoints (Orb/Metronome SDKs do); that is an SDK ergonomics item, not a platform change. No patch to the endpoints.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Lists return up to 100 records per page with a cursor to fetch the next page — standard practice that matches Metronome, and nothing is hidden. The only follow-up is making sure the SDK pages through automatically for the customer.

- Platform-fee config (`ProductFeeConfig` / `BillingTenantConfig`) has no tenant-facing API — tenants can SEE periods/invoices but not their fee schedule terms; platform-fee invoices are hardcoded usd regardless of tenant `default_currency` (ubb-platform/apps/billing/stripe/services/stripe_service.py:195).

  > **Verified —** True. No route in `tenant_endpoints.py` reads or writes `ProductFeeConfig`/`BillingTenantConfig` — tenants get `list_billing_periods`/`list_invoices` (which surface `platform_fee_micros`) but never the fee schedule terms themselves. The platform-fee invoice item is hardcoded `currency="usd"` (stripe_service.py:195) regardless of the tenant's `default_currency` (models.py:49).
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Two issues. (a) No fee-terms read API: this is partly deliberate (the fee is UBB's pricing toward the tenant, operator-controlled — see the immutability of `platform_fee_percentage` two bullets up), but tenants seeing the resulting `platform_fee_micros` without the rate that produced it is a transparency gap; the low-ripple fix is a read-only `GET /platform-fee` returning the effective schedule (no write). (b) The hardcoded `usd` is a genuine correctness bug for non-USD tenants — UBB itself supports multi-currency (`default_currency`, CUR-1 currency-lock at tenant_endpoints.py:339-371), and Orb requires items mapped to the right Stripe currency or "invoices will fail to issue" (03 Orb, docs.withorb.com/.../stripe). Fix: drive the platform-fee invoice currency from the tenant's billing currency rather than the literal `"usd"` at stripe_service.py:195 (verify the tenant's UBB-side Stripe customer is denominated to match). Contained to `stripe_service.py`.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Customers can see what we charged them in platform fees but not the rate behind it, and worse, those fee invoices are always issued in US dollars even for non-dollar customers — a real bug. Read-only fee transparency is a nice-to-have; the hardcoded currency should be fixed.

- OpenAPI docs UIs and specs are publicly reachable (no auth/docs_decorator) at every mount's `/docs` + `/openapi.json` — an information exposure to consider before production (ninja defaults, ubb-platform/.venv/Lib/site-packages/ninja/main.py:58-61; no overrides in the repo).

  > **Verified —** True. ninja's defaults are `openapi_url="/openapi.json"` and `docs_url="/docs"` (ninja/main.py:58-61), and a grep for `docs_url`/`docs_decorator`/`openapi_url` across `ubb-platform/api/` returns NO matches — no NinjaAPI instance overrides them. Every mount in `config/urls.py` (lines 21-41) therefore exposes its Swagger UI + spec unauthenticated.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is a real information-exposure to fix before production. The competitive norm is a single published, intentional spec (Orb publishes one spec at api.withorb.com/spec.json; 03 Orb) rather than a live unauthenticated Swagger UI per internal mount leaking the full surface. The fix is small and self-contained: set `docs_url=None` (and optionally `openapi_url=None`) on each NinjaAPI in production — driven off a `settings.DEBUG`/env flag so docs stay on in dev — or wrap them with a `docs_decorator` requiring auth. Touches each `NinjaAPI(...)` constructor (api/v1 endpoints, tenant/sandbox/metering/billing/subscriptions/margin/referrals/webhook/platform/connect) plus a settings flag; no model/migration. Keep docs available in dev; disable in prod.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Right now anyone on the internet can browse our full interactive API docs and schema without logging in — fine in development, but it hands attackers a map in production. The fix is a one-line per-API switch to turn docs off (or behind auth) when deployed live.

- The platform_api endpoints (customers/plans/subscribe/seats/lifecycle) carry no product gate — ApiKeyAuth only (ubb-platform/api/v1/platform_endpoints.py:34) — while the subscriptions read API requires the `subscriptions` product entitlement (ubb-platform/apps/subscriptions/api/endpoints.py:34).

  > **Verified —** True. `platform_api = NinjaAPI(auth=ApiKeyAuth(), ...)` (platform_endpoints.py:34) — no product gate; `create_customer` and siblings run on any valid key. By contrast `subscriptions_api` builds `_product_check = ProductAccess("subscriptions")` (endpoints.py:34) and gates its routes on the `subscriptions` entitlement. So orchestration writes (customers/plans/subscribe/seats/lifecycle) are reachable without the entitlement the read API requires — an inconsistency.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** This is an internal entitlement-consistency gap rather than a competitor-differentiated one (Metronome scopes tokens by endpoint, 03 Metronome, but that's key-scoping not product-entitlement). The concern is real: a tenant without the `subscriptions` product can create subscription/seat objects via `platform_api` that it cannot then read via `subscriptions_api`, and the orchestration writes arguably mutate billing-product state. Fix is low-ripple and mirrors the existing pattern: add `ProductAccess("subscriptions")` (or `"billing"`, per the product model) to the subscribe/seats/lifecycle routes on `platform_api`, leaving pure customer-CRUD ungated if that's intended. Decide deliberately which `platform_api` verbs require which product; enforce via the same `ProductAccess` dependency already used at endpoints.py:34. No schema change.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** A customer can create subscriptions and seats through one API even without the subscriptions add-on that's required to read them back — an internal inconsistency. We should gate the orchestration write endpoints on the same entitlement, using the product-check we already have.

- Health checks are fixed to database + redis; no Celery or Stripe checks (ubb-platform/api/v1/endpoints.py:16-38).

  > **Verified —** True. `/health` (endpoints.py:11-13) is a static `{"status":"ok"}`; `/ready` (lines 16-38) checks only `connection.ensure_connection()` (database) and a Redis `ping()`, returning 503 if either fails. No Celery worker/beat liveness check and no Stripe reachability check.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Best practice for a billing system whose correctness depends on async workers (outbox delivery, reconcilers, the 5-min `last_used_at` flush, sandbox reset) is for readiness to reflect the critical async path, not just the datastores — Orb publishes per-component health including Ingest/Webhooks/Invoicing (03 Orb status page), implying each subsystem is independently monitored. The gap: if Celery is down, `/ready` still returns 200 while webhooks and reconciliation silently stall. Fix: add a Celery liveness probe to `/ready` (e.g. `app.control.ping(timeout=...)` or a heartbeat key written by beat and checked for freshness) as an additional check in the existing `checks` dict. Do NOT add a live Stripe API call to `/ready` (it would make readiness depend on a third party and invite flapping) — monitor Stripe via a separate, non-gating synthetic check. Contained to `endpoints.py`.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Our health check confirms the database and Redis are up but not that the background workers are running — so webhooks and billing reconciliation could be stalled while we still report "healthy." Adding a worker liveness check closes that blind spot; we should not put Stripe in the health check itself.


### 5.6 SDK gaps & footguns

- `UBBClient.withdraw` delegates to `/debit` (not `/withdraw`): bypasses the insufficient-balance check, promo-exclusion, and the `billing.withdrawal_requested` event, and can overdraw (ubb-sdk/ubb/client.py:501-514, its docstring says so). `UBBClient.refund_usage` delegates to `/credit` (not `/refund`): credits the caller-supplied amount as a plain ADJUSTMENT, bypassing lot-aware re-funding and `refund.requested` (client.py:516-530). `BillingClient` exposes neither real endpoint.

  > **Verified — True, and the refund bug is worse than a wrong endpoint — it refunds $0.** Confirmed by reading the code exactly. `UBBClient.withdraw` (client.py:501-514) calls `billing.debit(...)` → `POST /api/v1/billing/debit`, whose own docstring admits "the billing client doesn't have a dedicated withdraw endpoint yet." The real `/customers/{id}/withdraw` (billing_endpoints.py:201-252) does the insufficient-balance check (`balance - promo_remaining < amount` → 400), excludes promo from withdrawable, and emits `WithdrawalRequested`; `/debit` does none of that and can drive the balance negative. `UBBClient.refund_usage` (client.py:516-530) calls `billing.credit(customer, amount_micros=0, source="refund", ...)` → `POST /credit` — it passes a HARD-CODED **zero amount**, so it credits the customer NOTHING. The prior reviewer is CORRECT. The real `/customers/{id}/refund` (billing_endpoints.py:268-335) looks the event's cost up server-side via `get_usage_event_cost` (298) and does lot-aware re-funding. Note both real endpoints key the customer by PK `id`, whereas the SDK debit/credit pass `external_id` — the rewrite must use the customer's UUID path.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** These are SDK-only bugs (no server migration; the correct endpoints already exist and are tested). Exact fix: rewrite `withdraw` to `billing._request("post", f"/api/v1/billing/customers/{id}/withdraw", json={"amount_micros":..., "idempotency_key":..., "description":...})`, and `refund_usage` to POST `/customers/{id}/refund` with `{"usage_event_id":..., "idempotency_key":..., "reason":...}` (no amount — the server computes it). Add a `withdraw()`/`refund()` pair on `BillingClient` so the real endpoints are reachable directly. Ripple is confined to client.py + billing.py + a resolve-external-id-to-UUID step.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Two money commands in the SDK are broken: "withdraw" can overdraw a wallet because it skips the balance check, and "refund" gives the customer back exactly zero dollars. Both are pure SDK bugs — the correct, safe server endpoints already exist and just need to be wired up. Fix before anyone touches real money.

- `UBBClient.record_usage` (facade) cannot send `usage_metrics` or `recorded_at` and makes `provider_cost_micros` mandatory — engine-priced or backfilled ingestion must use `client.metering.record_usage` directly (ubb-sdk/ubb/client.py:156-188).

  > **Verified — True.** client.py:156-188: the facade signature makes `provider_cost_micros` a required keyword (no default) and exposes no `usage_metrics` or `recorded_at` params, forwarding only the scalar set to `metering.record_usage`. The full-power method `MeteringClient.record_usage` (metering.py:100-148) does take `usage_metrics` and `recorded_at`. So engine-priced ingestion (omit cost, let rate cards compute) and backdated ingestion are impossible through the facade — you must drop to `client.metering.record_usage`. Confirmed; matches the doc and the §3.1.1 note.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** No 03 competitor fact bears on this convenience-wrapper shape, so it is best-practice framing. The risk is a footgun, not a money bug: a tenant using the obvious top-level helper silently cannot do named-metric (rate-card) pricing or backfills. Fix is mechanical: widen the facade to `provider_cost_micros: int | None = None`, add `usage_metrics` and `recorded_at` kwargs, and pass them through — the lower-level client already validates naive datetimes. One-file change in client.py; no server impact.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** The easy one-line way to record usage in the SDK forces you to supply your own cost and can't use the rate-card pricing engine or backdate events — the very features the product is built around. The full capability is there one layer down; the shortcut should simply expose it too.

- SDK debit/credit never send an `idempotency_key` (not replay-safe) (ubb-sdk/ubb/billing.py:80-236).

  > **Verified — True.** billing.py:80-98: `debit` posts only `{customer_id, amount_micros, reference}` and `credit` only `{customer_id, amount_micros, source, reference}` — neither includes an `idempotency_key`. Crucially, the SERVER side supports it: `/debit` (billing_endpoints.py:70-75) and `/credit` (114-119) both short-circuit on a matching `WalletTransaction.idempotency_key` and return the original transaction. So the replay protection exists server-side and the SDK simply never opts in — a network retry of a debit double-charges.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Strong competitor evidence this is below bar: Orb's SDKs include "built-in support for idempotency" and its general API idempotency-key is "strongly encouraged for all POST/PATCH requests" (03 Orb); Metronome documents an `Idempotency-Key` header cached ">= 24 hours" and SDKs that auto-retry (03 Metronome). Retrying a non-idempotent write is exactly what those keys prevent. Fix is SDK-only: add an `idempotency_key: str` param to `BillingClient.debit`/`credit` and include it in the JSON body (the server already honors it). Since the SDK retries 429/502/503/504 automatically (retry.py), shipping debit/credit without a key is actively dangerous; consider making the key required.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** When the SDK debits or credits a wallet and the network hiccups, a retry can charge twice — because the SDK omits the "do this only once" key that the server already understands. Competitors make idempotency standard on every write. This is a one-line-per-method SDK fix with no server change.

- The SDK `CustomerMargin` dataclass silently drops API fields (`revenue_mode`, `usage_revenue_micros`, `total_revenue_micros`, `event_count`) (ubb-sdk/ubb/metering.py:262-264; ubb-sdk/ubb/types.py:133-140).

  > **Verified — True.** types.py:133-140: `CustomerMargin` declares only `customer_id, subscription_revenue_micros, usage_billed_micros, provider_cost_micros, gross_margin_micros, margin_percentage`. metering.py:260-264: `get_customer_margin` constructs it with `{k: v ... if k in CustomerMargin.__dataclass_fields__}` — so any response field NOT in that frozen set (the doc names `revenue_mode`, `usage_revenue_micros`, `total_revenue_micros`, `event_count`) is silently discarded with no error. Confirmed: the filter is exactly the silent-drop mechanism the bullet describes.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** No direct 03 fact, but Orb/Metronome both advertise "strong typing" in their SDKs (03) — the expectation is that the typed object mirrors the API, not a lossy subset. Given UBB's own margin model distinguishes earned/accrual revenue (revenue_mode, usage_revenue_micros, total_revenue_micros), dropping those means an SDK consumer can't see the revenue-recognition basis that the platform works hard to compute. SDK-only fix: add the four fields to the `CustomerMargin` dataclass (Optional, defaulted) so the existing `__dataclass_fields__` filter passes them through automatically. No endpoint or server change. Audit `DimensionMargin`/`MarginTrendPoint` for the same pattern while there.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** The SDK's margin object quietly throws away several numbers the server sends — including how revenue was recognized — so analytics built on it are blind to data that exists. Adding the missing fields to one dataclass restores them; nothing else changes.

- No SDK wrapper for: sandbox reset (POST `/api/v1/sandbox/reset`), webhook-config CRUD, tenant billing-periods/invoices, `/margin/summary`, the `/margin` list, or `/margin/threshold` — raw HTTP needed (auditor greps of ubb-sdk found no matches).

  > **Verified — True, with a precision note.** Grep of metering.py confirms the SDK wraps `/margin/{id}`, `/by-dimension`, `/unprofitable`, `/{id}/trend`, revenue, business, and revenue-mode — but NOT `/margin/summary`, the bare `/margin` list, or `/margin/threshold`. No webhook-config CRUD wrappers exist (the SDK has only verify_webhook/verify_webhook_legacy, which are signature verification, not config management), and no tenant billing-periods/invoices wrapper. **Precision note on "sandbox reset":** `UBBClient` DOES have `create_sandbox`/`get_sandbox`, but those hit `POST/GET /api/v1/tenant/sandbox` — they are NOT the `POST /api/v1/sandbox/reset` data-wipe endpoint the bullet names, which genuinely has no wrapper. So the bullet is accurate; the only nuance is that adjacent sandbox-provisioning verbs do exist.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** Best-practice framing (no specific 03 fact). Competitor SDKs are positioned as full API surface coverage (Orb publishes an OpenAPI spec "for generating clients in other languages"; both Orb and Metronome ship typed multi-language SDKs — 03), so leaving operability endpoints raw-HTTP-only is a coverage gap, not a money risk. Fix: add thin wrappers — `reset_sandbox()`, webhook-config CRUD (create/list/delete), `get_billing_periods()`/`get_invoices()`, and the three missing margin reads — each a few lines reusing the existing `_request` helper. Pure additive SDK work; no server change.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** Several admin and reporting endpoints have no SDK shortcut, so integrators must hand-write raw HTTP for them. It's a polish/coverage gap, not a correctness problem — competitors aim for full-surface SDKs, and these are quick additive wrappers.

- `SubscriptionsClient` is read/sync-only (`sync`, `get_subscription`, `get_invoices` — ubb-sdk/ubb/subscriptions.py:76-93); ALL write verbs live on `UBBClient` and ride the metering product client.

  > **Verified — True.** subscriptions.py:74-93 exposes exactly three methods: `sync` (POST /subscriptions/sync), `get_subscription` (GET), `get_invoices` (GET) — no create/cancel/pause/resume/seats writers. Confirmed those write verbs instead live on `UBBClient` (`subscribe_customer`, `cancel_subscription`, `pause_subscription`, `resume_subscription`, `set_seats`, `create_plan`, `update_plan`), and each rides metering's HTTP client via `self.metering._request` against `/api/v1/platform/...` (client.py:247-332). So a tenant who instantiates only `subscriptions=True` cannot perform any subscription write — the writes require the metering product to be enabled. Matches the doc.
  >
  > **Competitors & the fix —** No 03 fact on competitor SDK module layout, so this is best-practice framing. It's an ergonomics/coupling oddity rather than a bug: subscription lifecycle lives under the platform API surface (which is API-key-only, no product gate per §5.5), so routing writes through the metering client is an internal implementation detail that leaks into the SDK's shape. Optional fix: add the write verbs to `SubscriptionsClient` (delegating to the same platform endpoints) so the class name matches its capability, or document clearly that subscription writes are facade-level on `UBBClient`. SDK-only; no server change.
  >
  > **In plain terms —** The SDK's "Subscriptions" client can only read and sync, never create or cancel — all the write actions live on the main client and quietly depend on the metering module being on. It works, but the naming misleads; tidying it is cosmetic SDK work.
